    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer1849588115190832906">Ambrose Young was beautiful. He was tall and muscular, with hair that touched his shoulders and eyes that burned right through you. The kind of beautiful that graced the covers of romance novels, and Fern Taylor would know. She'd been reading them since she was thirteen. But maybe because he was so beautiful he was never someone Fern thought she could have . . . until he w</span>
  <span id="freeText1849588115190832906" style="display:none">Ambrose Young was beautiful. He was tall and muscular, with hair that touched his shoulders and eyes that burned right through you. The kind of beautiful that graced the covers of romance novels, and Fern Taylor would know. She'd been reading them since she was thirteen. But maybe because he was so beautiful he was never someone Fern thought she could have . . . until he wasn't beautiful anymore. Making Faces is the story of a small town where five young men go off to war, and only one comes back. It is the story of loss. Collective loss, individual loss, loss of beauty, loss of life, loss of identity. It is the tale of one girl's love for a broken boy and a wounded warrior's love for an unremarkable girl. This is a story of friendship that overcomes heartache, heroism that defies the common definitions, and a modern tale of Beauty and the Beast, where we discover that there is a little beauty and a little beast in all of us.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1849588115190832906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is no actual sex or drugs in this book. My daughter is 11 and if she asked I would let her read it. There aren't topics in here that she and I h<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is no actual sex or drugs in this book. My daughter is 11 and if she asked I would let her read it. There aren't topics in here that she and I have never discussed. I don't know if she would enjoy it yet though. The biggest message from this book is to be the best you you can be and love who you are and be good inside and out. I'm in my 30's and enjoyed it. So I wouldn't put an end age on it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=6-star-books">6-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744992042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1456700665660034377"><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382403400i/5868751._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382380089i/5858111.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Here's my casting for Ambrose^^^<br/><br/>** FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED **<br/><br/><b> Absolutely breathtaking! 5 stars!! ★★★★★<br/><br/>This book blew me away!! It was beautifully written and deeply moving, with a very powerful message about true beauty, silver linings, and second chances. A poignant and unconventional tale about heroism, courage, love, loss, friendship, and self-acceptance.  </b><br/><br/>Every once in a while a book comes a long that, from the moment I first hear about it, takes over my mind and heart and doesn't let go unti</span>
  <span id="freeText1456700665660034377" style="display:none"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382403400i/5868751._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382380089i/5858111.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Here's my casting for Ambrose^^^<br><br>** FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED **<br><br><b> Absolutely breathtaking! 5 stars!! ★★★★★<br><br>This book blew me away!! It was beautifully written and deeply moving, with a very powerful message about true beauty, silver linings, and second chances. A poignant and unconventional tale about heroism, courage, love, loss, friendship, and self-acceptance.  </b><br><br>Every once in a while a book comes a long that, from the moment I first hear about it, takes over my mind and heart and doesn't let go until I've read it, lived it and immersed myself in the story. <em>Making Faces</em> was such a book. I read the blurb and shivers just went right through me and I immediately knew that this book was a must-read.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“Making Faces is the story of a small town where five young men go off to war, and only one comes back… It is the tale of one girl’s love for a broken boy, and a wounded warrior’s love for an unremarkable girl. This is a story of friendship that overcomes heartache, heroism that defies the common definitions, and a modern tale of Beauty and the Beast, where we discover that there is a little beauty and a little beast in all of us.” </i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>See?? Tell me that doesn't make you want to drop everything and read this?!<br><br>Once I started reading, I could not put this book down and it kept me riveted to the page until I finished at 4AM. It captivated me from start to finish and stayed with my heart long after I had turned the last page.<br><br>The heroine, Fern, had been in love with Ambrose from the time they were kids. Problem was, he barely knew she existed - at least, not in the way she wanted. He was the school's star athlete and she was just a shy, forgettable girl who never imaged that anyone as handsome as him would ever take notice of her.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <em>“If God makes all our faces, did he laugh when he made me?”</em>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>When Ambrose enlisted following the crushing events of 9/11, he left with four of his best friends but was the only one to come home alive and even so, a part of him wished he'd died with them. Broken, permanently wounded, and guilt-ridden he hid himself from the world. But it was the love of a quiet but fiercely strong girl that helped bring him back to life and learn that there is always a silver lining and that everyone deserved a second chance.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <em>"I used to be afraid of going to hell. But now that I'm here, hell doesn't seem so bad."</em>
    <br>
    <br>
    <em>"Sometimes you can't take your life back. Sometimes it's dead and buried and you can only make a new life."</em>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>Part of what struck me about this book was that it felt completely 'different' than anything else I'd read. Unique. Fresh. This was not a story I'd already read twenty times and despite the fact that it did carry some well-known themes, it's delivery was heartfelt and original.<br><br>It's more than just a romance too (in fact, there is no graphic sex in it) and it's just as much about friendship as it is about love. I don't want to spoil things for you but the balance between all the different elements of this story were perfect. Many parts were so heart breaking that I just read with tears pouring down my face, while others filled me with such happiness that I'd read page after page with a huge smile.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <em>"How did you know I needed you?"<br>"Because I needed you too."</em>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>The book brought out emotion after emotion from me. It's such a strong, character driven story and it's the kind where every single section has a little message or life lesson or something that just makes you take a step back and think about it for a minute. It's not only beautifully written but it's also very well crafted and even the simplest of phrases carry rich, multi-layered meaning.<br><br>Everything about this story is somehow connected. As a result of it taking place over so many years, we got to see how little seemingly insignificant details came into play later on in a powerful, life-changing way.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <em>"We all fit together to create this experience we call life. None of us can see the part we play or the way it all turns out. Maybe the miracles that we see are just the tip of the iceberg. And maybe we just don't recognize the blessings that come as a result of terrible things."</em>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>It brought up so many questions and things to ponder... Why was someone born a certain way? Why did someone survive? Was there a grand design? Or was it all just random chance handed out by the universe?<br><br>There is so much more to the story that I've decided not to talk about in my review because I didn't know any more than I've told you at this point when I started reading and I absolutely <em>loved</em> the process of just watching the story unfold and not fully knowing what to expect. Just know that I do not have a <em>single</em> complaint about this book. Not one. Just trust me and read it. I promise you will not be disappointed.<br><br>By the end of the book, tears were streaming down my face - a true testament to the overwhelming emotions it pulled out of me. The ending, the last line in particular, was just <em>perfect!!! </em>Like I said.... breathtaking!<br><br>This is now one of my favorites of the year!<br><br>
  <strong>Everyone should read this book</strong>
. This is the kind of unforgettable story that sinks into your heart and doesn't let go. I can't recommend it highly enough.<br><br>5 stars!!<br><br>This is a standalone (complete with epilogue).<br><br>****************************<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1456700665660034377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1738822419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4705672589810842037"><b>Let Me Just . . .</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472236730ra/20171155.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467375581ra/19585234.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>The end of this book broke my heart and made me rage. Okay, the very end was a good ending. But before that I just, there was, WAIT . . .</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465480303ra/19362800.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467375581ra/19585234.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>So in this book I loved many characters but my favorites were Fern, Bailey and Ambrose. Fern and Bailey are cousins who live next door to each other. Bailey has muscular dystropy and Fern helps him in anything he needs. They are wonderful characters and funny and smart and dorks and I loved them. I wanted to be their best friend. Yes, I say th</span>
  <span id="freeText4705672589810842037" style="display:none"><b>Let Me Just . . .</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472236730ra/20171155.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467375581ra/19585234.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The end of this book broke my heart and made me rage. Okay, the very end was a good ending. But before that I just, there was, WAIT . . .</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465480303ra/19362800.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467375581ra/19585234.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>So in this book I loved many characters but my favorites were Fern, Bailey and Ambrose. Fern and Bailey are cousins who live next door to each other. Bailey has muscular dystropy and Fern helps him in anything he needs. They are wonderful characters and funny and smart and dorks and I loved them. I wanted to be their best friend. Yes, I say that a lot in books! I get really involved in my books and the characters. Don't judge me! <br><br>Anyway, so Fern falls in love with Ambrose for the first time when she meets him as a child. He came over and crushed a spider outside that Fern and Bailey were watching. He thought they were afraid of it and didn't understand why Bailey went inside crying. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Bailey has a disease. It makes his muscles weak. It might kill him. He doesn't like it when things die. It's hard for him," Fern said simply, honestly. She actually sounded kinda smart. Suddenly, the events at the wrestling camp earlier that summer made sense to Ambrose. Bailey wasn't supposed to wrestle because he had a disease. Ambrose felt bad all over again.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>As you have guessed, Ambrose is on the wrestling team at school. He ends up being a star and wins a scholarship to go to college. But he has other plans. He talks 4 of his teammates so sign up for the military and that is what they do. They were in school when 9/11 happened and Ambrose wants to do something other than try to be a star for everyone. <br><br>Fern has been reading romance books since she was young and she has been writing her own books in private for just as long. Only Bailey knows that she's trying to get a book deal, well until Ambrose finds out later on. <br><br>Fern has another best friend named Rita and at one point in their school days Rita wants to get together with Ambrose. She doesn't know that Fern is crushing on him so she asks her to write some notes to Ambrose - because Fern can write good stuff. Well, we all know that backfires when Ambrose starts to care for Rita, writing back beautiful things and then finds out Rita and Fern were tricking him. He didn't talk to them much after that! <br><br>So off to war they go and the book goes back and forth from the present to some things that happened in the past but it's not confusing at all. When Ambrose returns home a year or two later from a horrific tragedy, he's not the same. He goes back to work in his father's bakery which is in the grocery where Fern works until midnight. She tries to become friends with him again. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>In black letters she wrote KITES OR BALLOONS across the whiteboard, and she taped a red balloon, his favorite color, to the side. He would know it was Fern. Once upon a time, they had asked each other a million questions just like this. In fact, Ambrose had been the first to ask this particular question. Kites or balloons? Fern has said kites because if she were a kite she could fly, but someone would always be holding onto her. Ambrose had said balloons: "I like the idea of flying away and letting the wind take me. I don't think I want anyone holding onto me." Fern wondered if his response would be the same now as it had been then.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Gradually, Fern and Bailey bring Ambrose out of hiding. He didn't want the world to see him. He felt like a beast and he felt it was his fault for a lot of things that happened. But the three started having a wonderful time together. How could you not with Fern and Bailey! <br><br>But there are more tragedies and the book just broke my little heart. I don't want to do any spoilers for this book because this is one that you should read for yourself. The feels and just . . . the everything. Even though there were things that brought me to my knees in this book, I did love it. Just know that if you read it, bring the tissues and if you have no reaction to some of the stuff then I wonder if your human? <br><br>Oh and there was one thing at the end that had me happy crying too ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/08/making-faces-by-amy-harmon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_720694089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/720694089" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/720694089?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs">Amy | Foxy Blogs</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=weepy">weepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=epic-profound">epic-profound</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=powerful">powerful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer720694089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9429798136804115694"><b>*5+++ Stars!*<br/><br/>A touching portrayal of not only finding beauty within, but of finding the beauty within the ugly...</b><br/><br/>There's <i>so</i> much beauty to be found in this story, and not nearly enough words to adequately honor it. This book starts off simple — discreet even — with an undeniable <b>depth</b> and <b>wisdom</b> that slowly sneaks up and consumes you. Its incredible insight is gently suggested, but powerfully received. With an expertly smooth execution, this author makes it all seem entirely effortless as she st</span>
  <span id="freeText9429798136804115694" style="display:none"><b>*5+++ Stars!*<br><br>A touching portrayal of not only finding beauty within, but of finding the beauty within the ugly...</b><br><br>There's <i>so</i> much beauty to be found in this story, and not nearly enough words to adequately honor it. This book starts off simple — discreet even — with an undeniable <b>depth</b> and <b>wisdom</b> that slowly sneaks up and consumes you. Its incredible insight is gently suggested, but powerfully received. With an expertly smooth execution, this author makes it all seem entirely effortless as she strips down life to its bare components, revealing the grace from within. I fell in love with these lovingly broken and perfectly flawed characters, who each represented a unique piece of the same puzzle. <br><br><b>Fern</b> is the girl who feels her plain and unattractive physical appearance renders her insignificant. She clings to the comfort of being "invisible", until she finally decides she WANTS to be <i>seen.</i> Her character has a quiet strength that was just as endearing as her vulnerability. She's genuinely easy to love, but had difficulty recognizing her worth. She's also in love with Ambrose—the boy who doesn't seem to "see" her at all. <br><br><b>Ambrose</b> is the competent, gorgeous star athlete who's drowning in the pressures and expectations of always having to <i>win.</i> When his need to escape lands him in the military during war, Ambrose suffers a tragedy as well as an injury that permanently deforms his beautiful face ... leaving him forever changed as he hides from the people back home. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>I'm not ashamed to be seen with you. I'm ashamed to be seen.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><b>Bailey</b> is Fern's cousin who suffers the crippling effects of muscular dystrophy. His love of life and ability to live freely in the moment overshadowed his physical shortcomings to the point where I was drawing strength from his character. But the one thing Bailey desperately wanted was to be a <b>hero</b> ... like Ambrose. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Victory is in the battle...</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The love story of Fern and Ambrose was on another level than most. It didn't rely on angst or steam as its motivation, but gradually came alive through a deeper, more meaningful connection. There were strong religious and spiritual undertones that strengthened this story's messages without becoming preachy or judgmental. The writing was phenomenal, symbolic, fresh, and original — and I loved that poetry so heavily influenced this plot. <br><br>I must admit that this story's raw power and heartbreaking scenarios had me in an almost constant fit of tears. But it was a beautiful cry fest. I cried for a Fern — for believing she was so incredibly insignificant because of her unremarkable appearance. I cried for Ambrose's quiet strength, humility, and decency—which was all I saw in both his beautiful and "beastly" state. And for Bailey — who so desperately craved becoming a hero, never realizing he was one all along. <br><br>All of that being said, this book honestly made me <b>happy.</b> It truly exemplified how beauty is not found with the eye, and how strength is not only measured by physical endurance; How we can often become more perceptive as a result of what we <i>lack</i> rather than what we <i>have</i>. It showed that even heroes falter, and proved how tremendous tragedies can be transformed into the greatest of blessings —depending upon on how you perceive them. <br><br><b>
  <u>I'll end with a poem, written by Fern — felt by many:</u>
  <br>
  <i>
    <blockquote>If God made all our faces, did he laugh when he made me?<br>Does he make the legs that cannot walk and eyes that cannot see?<br>Does he curl the hair upon my head 'til it rebels in wild defiance?<br>Does he close the ears of a deaf man to make him more reliant?<br><br>Is the way I look a coincidence or just a twist of fate?<br>If he made me this way, is it okay, to blame him for the things I hate?<br>For the flaws that seem to worsen every time I see a mirror,<br>For the ugliness I see in me, for the loathing and the fear.<br><br>Does he sculpt us for his pleasure, for a reason I can't see?<br>If God makes all our faces, did he laugh when he made me?</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪	 Genre/Category:</b> Romance/NA<br><b>▪	 Steam Caliber:</b> Clean but passionate and sexy.<br><b>▪ Romance:</b> Beautiful and angst fee. Slow build.<br><b>▪	 Characters:</b> Layered. Flawed. Unique and beautiful. <br><b>▪	 Plot:</b> Centers on finding and loving the beauty within.<br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Unique, engaging, fluid, flawless. Weaves through past and present.<br><b>▪ POV:</b> 3rd Person Perspective. <br><b>▪	 Cliffhanger:</b> None/Standalone<br><b>▪ HEA? </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="http://prettywordsbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412050368i/11316768.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_875762133" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/875762133" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/875762133?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18721737-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dark-themes">dark-themes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=sweet-heart-warming-stories">sweet-heart-warming-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer875762133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6428433430098269485">This book had been on my radar for a long time. Let me say that I have never read an Amy Harmon book that I didn't love. So why did I put off reading this one for so long? Well, I honestly just wasn't ready to suffer another heartache at the hands of this incredibly talented author. Her books are always beautiful, but highly emotional. I have to be in the right frame of mind to dive into one of her books, with my tissues handy and ready to shed a few tears.<br/><br/>As expected, 'Making Faces' was exactly</span>
  <span id="freeText6428433430098269485" style="display:none">This book had been on my radar for a long time. Let me say that I have never read an Amy Harmon book that I didn't love. So why did I put off reading this one for so long? Well, I honestly just wasn't ready to suffer another heartache at the hands of this incredibly talented author. Her books are always beautiful, but highly emotional. I have to be in the right frame of mind to dive into one of her books, with my tissues handy and ready to shed a few tears.<br /><br />As expected, 'Making Faces' was exactly the type of emotion-evoking read that she is so well known for. It was equal parts tragic and inspirational. It was a breathtakingly beautiful journey, with a lot of loss and heartache along the way. <br /><br />Ambrose Young is the kind of guy that everybody loves. The guys want to be him and the girls just want him. He's the high school wrestling star, destined to do great things. On top of that, he's extremely attractive and popular. Yet, there is a softer, more romantic side to Ambrose that few people ever get to see.<br /><br />Fern Taylor is the daughter of a pastor. She's somewhat sheltered and definitely not the life of the party, like Ambrose. Fern shies away from the spotlight, choosing to spend her time reading and hanging out with her cousin, Bailey, who suffers from Muscular Dystrophy.<br /><br />Despite their differences, Fern and Ambrose form a strong bond when Fern begins penning love letters to her long-time crush. However, Fern isn't honest with Ambrose, pretending to be her best friend. When her deceit is revealed, Ambrose feels betrayed and shuns Fern.<br /><br />As their high school years come to a close, Fern and Ambrose eventually find their way back to one another. However, their relationship is over before it ever has a chance to take off. Ambrose is enlisting in the armed services, along with several of his friends, and is set to leave town soon.<br /><br />When Ambrose returns, he is permanently changed. After an attack that left his closest friends dead, he lives with severe facial deformities and scarring. He is haunted by the traumatic events day and night. To make matters worse, he is the object of scorn for some of the parents that lost their children. He has become the target of their anger, a role he embraces.<br /><br />Eventually, Fern and Ambrose cross paths again. Fern is initially shocked by the appearance of the boy that she spent so many years fantasizing about. Getting over the initial surprise, she is determined to reach out to Ambrose and find the goodness that she knows lives within him. As determined as he is to fade into obscurity, she is persistent and gradually works her way back into his life.<br /><br />As Fern and Ambrose grow closer, the lives of their friends grow more complicated. Bailey lives with the pain of watching the girl he loves endure a living hell. His light-hearted presence in Fern and Ambrose's lives is in direct contrast to the sadness he lives with.<br /><br />While this book was not particularly surprising, I absolutely loved it. It was everything that I expected from Amy Harmon. I fell in love with these characters and could not stop listening to this story. I listened to the entire book, straight through, in one day. I was absolutely consumed by it. Hands-down, this is one of my best reads for the year! I loved it!<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6428433430098269485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_720684223" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/720684223" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/720684223?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer720684223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13672928048226885667"><b>More than 5 Stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/887fe008-84ea-4cd1-a9a6-fed7884004ca_zps904f851e.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247944.jpg' alt=' photo 887fe008-84ea-4cd1-a9a6-fed7884004ca_zps904f851e.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Wow... just wow! This is one of those special books I wish I could give extra stars to- 5 stars, it just doesn’t seem adequate. When I read a story like this, it’s hard to put it into words how I feel. This book blew me away. One of the very best books I’ve read this year! <br/><br/>Fern Taylor and Ambrose Young... <br/><br/>Fern is that awkward girl. Red hair, freckles, glasses, braces. She loves to read, takes care of her best friend and cousin, Bailey, and remains closed off to most. Those </span>
  <span id="freeText13672928048226885667" style="display:none"><b>More than 5 Stars!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/887fe008-84ea-4cd1-a9a6-fed7884004ca_zps904f851e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247944.jpg" alt=" photo 887fe008-84ea-4cd1-a9a6-fed7884004ca_zps904f851e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wow... just wow! This is one of those special books I wish I could give extra stars to- 5 stars, it just doesn’t seem adequate. When I read a story like this, it’s hard to put it into words how I feel. This book blew me away. One of the very best books I’ve read this year! <br><br>Fern Taylor and Ambrose Young... <br><br>Fern is that awkward girl. Red hair, freckles, glasses, braces. She loves to read, takes care of her best friend and cousin, Bailey, and remains closed off to most. Those who know her, those who she opens up to, know that she is one of the most beautiful people on the inside. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/2aee745b-3cee-406c-afcf-f21c8ec3a583_zpsd5a03025.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247945.jpg" alt=" photo 2aee745b-3cee-406c-afcf-f21c8ec3a583_zpsd5a03025.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Fern has been in love with Ambrose Young since they were children. Ambrose is the opposite of Fern. Even from a young age, he is beautiful, he is popular, he is kind. Everything about Ambrose is perfect to Fern, but like most people, he never really notices Fern. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/4b7d990f-2a17-4865-89c3-c5161b058d6f_zpsa45fe359.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247946.jpg" alt=" photo 4b7d990f-2a17-4865-89c3-c5161b058d6f_zpsa45fe359.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <blockquote>Could you belong to someone who didn’t want you? Fern decided it was possible because her heart was his, and whether or not he wanted it didn’t seem to make much difference.</blockquote>
</b><br>Fern and Ambrose connect in highschool in an unexpected way. Through letters. Ambrose doesn’t know that Fern is replying to his letters. He opens up to her more than he ever has with anyone. <br><i>
  <blockquote>
<u>‘Nobody or Nowhere?’</u><br>Fern: ‘I’d rather be nobody at home than somebody somewhere else.’<br>Ambrose:‘I’d rather be nowhere. Being nobody when your expected to be somebody gets old.’<br>Fern: ‘How would you know? Have you been nobody?’<br>Ambrose: ‘Everybody who is somebody becomes a nobody the moment they fail.’</blockquote>
</i><br>When Ambrose finds out it’s Fern, his feelings are conflicted. Although Ambrose appears to have it all, most popular guy in the school, star wrestler with a full scholarship to college, he feels all of that weighing on him much too heavily. After 9/11, Ambrose has felt he needed to do something. He wants to enlist. He talks to his four best friends, and they decide to go along with him. Five boys, from the same small town leaving for the Army. Fern stays in town after graduation. She works at the same store, continues reading and writing and hanging out with Bailey, but she always thinks of Ambrose.<br>Now that I’ve mentioned Bailey, let me talk about this very special character. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/669efbd9-4771-44a3-b9b5-9ce99f1e5a9a_zps4bf5e7de.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247947.jpg" alt=" photo 669efbd9-4771-44a3-b9b5-9ce99f1e5a9a_zps4bf5e7de.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As much as I loved Fern and Ambrose, Bailey was the very best part of this story. Bailey was so strong, so resolved to live his life to the very fullest. He was full of laughter, love and beauty. He was sweet, funny, and was exactly the person Fern needed in her life. I really agree with Fern’s mother and aunt. Fern and Bailey were brought into this world around the same time for each other. <br><br>I loved Bailey’s interactions with Fern:<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Do you think there’s any way someone like Ambrose could fall in love with someone like me?”<br> “Only if he’s lucky.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> He also had a special relationship with Ambrose. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Fern doesn’t have a clue how pretty she is. That makes her priceless. Make sure you snatch her up before she clues into her good looks, Brosey.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> Ambrose comes back from the war a changed man. He is different on the inside and the out. He has went through things, seen things he just can’t get past. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/9ec9891b-afda-4193-979d-d49815383e2b_zps03c605f0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247948.jpg" alt=" photo 9ec9891b-afda-4193-979d-d49815383e2b_zps03c605f0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As Fern comes into her self, she wants to help Ambrose come back to himself. Fern is resilient. She has such strength. She is lovely, has a way with words and has this passion to help those she cares for. Ambrose is drowning in guilt and sorrow. He is not the same man he once was. Fern (and even Bailey at times) bring him back. <br><i>
  <blockquote>We all fit together to create this experience we call life. None of us can see the part we play or the way it all turns out. Maybe the miracles we see are just the tip of the iceburg. And maybe we just don’t recognize the blessings that come as a result of terrible things.</blockquote>
</i><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/7a2e71f2-f997-4926-a663-68880e6b2bed_zpsd5ad62ba.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247949.jpg" alt=" photo 7a2e71f2-f997-4926-a663-68880e6b2bed_zpsd5ad62ba.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <blockquote>‘Victory is in the battle.’</blockquote>
</b> I can’t tell you how many times I cried while reading this...<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I’ll add you to my list.”<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“It wouldn’t hurt so badly if I didn’t love him so much. That’s the irony of it.” “There isn’t heartache if there hasn’t been joy. I wouldn’t feel loss if there hadn't been love.” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>But I also laughed, smiled and was just overwhelmed by the love I had for this story and these characters. One of my favorite parts towards the end...<br><b>
  <blockquote>‘When you get tired of looking at me, I promise I’ll sing.’</blockquote>
</b><br><br><i>Making Faces</i> was heartbreaking and heartwarming. Although there was sadness and loss, there was also much love, laughter and beauty. After reading <i>A Different Blue</i> by Amy Harmon, I knew when this came out I had to read it right away. What I didn’t know was how deeply it would effect me. This book moved me. Inspired me. Made me think, made me hope, made me feel. The writing was phenomenal, the story- one of a kind. Amazing, beautiful, the best kind of book. A story I will never forget. And it had the best message- true beauty, the kind that lasts comes from the inside of a person. I’ll leave you with this thought- Don't wait... if you haven't read this one yet, drop everything and pick it up!!!<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20reviews%203/6cc0d048-7922-49f4-b9a9-75738ed66c20_zpsdd592cb2.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382865983i/6247950.jpg" alt=" photo 6cc0d048-7922-49f4-b9a9-75738ed66c20_zpsdd592cb2.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

Maybe the miracles that we see are just the tip of the iceberg. And maybe we just don’t recognize the blessings that come as a result of terrible things."</b>

Apparently she’s some writer. Fern loves her. Unfortunately for Nora Roberts, she got knocked up and died giving birth."<br>"The writer?"<br>"No! The cat."</b>

You can have your pride and sit here and make cupcakes and get old and fat and nobody will give a damn after a while. Or you can trade that pride in for a little humility and take your life back.”</b>

It is the slow drip that makes the stalactite, the shaking of the Earth that creates mountains, the constant pounding of the waves that break up the rocks and smooths the rough edges. And from the violence, the furor, the raging of the winds, the roaring of the waters, something that would otherwise never exist. And so we endure. We have faith that there is a purpose. We hope for things we can’t see. We believe that there are lessons in loss, power in love, and that we have within us the potential for a beauty so magnificent that our bodies can’t contain it."</b>

<div id="review_1868791054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868791054" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1868791054?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1868791054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4541828158937239353"><b>HEART-BREAKING OR HEART-MENDING?</b><br/><br/>The answer is always the same when it comes to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon' title='Amy Harmon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amy Harmon</a>'s books. <b>Both</b>. I am not sure anything I'll say will do justice to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces' title='Making Faces by Amy Harmon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Making Faces</a>. It was a contradiction, sunny days swimming in a lake and nights full of nightmares, a song of <b>mourning</b> and <b>hope</b> that stirred a whirlwind of emotions that could be released only through tears, a lament and an ode to beauty. Beauty that can be found within, in caring, and giving and sharing. And honoring those you left behind by </span>
  <span id="freeText4541828158937239353" style="display:none"><b>HEART-BREAKING OR HEART-MENDING?</b><br><br>The answer is always the same when it comes to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a>'s books. <b>Both</b>. I am not sure anything I'll say will do justice to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces" title="Making Faces by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a>. It was a contradiction, sunny days swimming in a lake and nights full of nightmares, a song of <b>mourning</b> and <b>hope</b> that stirred a whirlwind of emotions that could be released only through tears, a lament and an ode to beauty. Beauty that can be found within, in caring, and giving and sharing. And honoring those you left behind by living life to the fullest. It was <b>inspirational</b>. Devastating. And undoubtedly, <b>soul-gripping.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497810540ra/23059218.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Death is easy. Living is the hard part.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>In a small Pensylvania town, a tight-knit community, remarkable things rarely happened. Until a September morning that paralyzed the U.S.A. and the entire world. The terrorist attack that left ruins, ashes and the blood of innocents was the trigger for Ambrose Young, the most promising wrestler, the pride of Hannah Lake, to be enlisted. To serve his country, and to avoid the burden of everyone's expectations. He didn't leave to war alone. He had his best friends by his side. But he did come back alone. Disfigured, drowning in guilt and sorrow. The man he was Before was gone.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If God made all our faces, did he laugh when he made me?” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Fern Taylor never stood out. She was just the daughter of the local pastor with fiery hair and a deep love for romances that everyone overlooked. But her heart was full of kindness. Her best friend and cousin, Bailey, was paralyzed due to a rare disease, but that didn't prevent him from enjoying life as best as he could, even though he was aware that death was waiting in the corner. Fern's days were simple. Take care of Bailey, read, write, and love Ambrose Young. Even when he ignored her. Even when was adamant he didn't deserve to be loved.<br><br><b>SORROW OR JOY?</b><br><br>Sorrow and joy, pain and love, all of them are interwined in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces" title="Making Faces by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a>. For there can be no pain and sorrow if you haven't experienced love and joy. That's what Amy Harmon tries to tell, through her <b>deeply endearing characters, the tragedies and the small and big moments of carelessness</b>. Making Faces is not about <i>one</i> love story. It's about <i>many</i> love stories, for love is endless. When I read this book, with reverence, with passion and compassion, I was not Katerina. I was Ambrose. Fern. Bailey. Rita. A mother mourning for her son. A pastor consoling his fold. A town burying her children. All that I was, all that I am, simply ceased to be. Amy Harmon shaped and reshaped me, poured her heart out on my empty canvas, and when my cheeks were wet and my heart slowly shattering, she wiped my tears with a tender caress and sang with a soft voice.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I wrote your name across my heart,<br>So we could be together<br>So I could hold you close to me<br>And keep you there forever.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>War. Survivor's guilt. Post traumatic stress disorder. Grief. Illness. Death. Pain.</b> Amy Harmon did not spare her characters. As if narrating a tale to a child, she crafted the lives of Ambrose, Fern and Bailey. Ambrose lost his friends. His self-esteem. His face. How do you get used to being ugly, meeting pity when you once were Hercules? When you were admired and worshiped and now you're just a pathetic shadow of your former self? But in his loneliness and devastation, Ambrose got closer to Fern and Bailey, <b>two adorable dorks</b>, the dying boy in the wheelchair and the girl who secretly loved him since they were kids and buried a spider in the yard. Fern thought that she was too plain, too ugly for Ambrose to notice her. Ambrose thought Fern was too good for him. But despite their doubts, a beautiful relationship blossomed between them, with the potential to lead to acceptance. Healing. The concept of beauty was thoroughly explored. Faith was questioned. Why God keeps sharing burdens and illness and death to people who don't deserve them? Are some lives more worthy than others? Are we all a piece of a puzzle, a greater picture we cannot see, or are we simply heading towards the ultimate end with no hope for something more?<br><br><b>UNDERSTANDING OR BELIEVING?</b><br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces" title="Making Faces by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a>, I understood the insecurities of a plain girl, a former demigod and a wannabe hero. And I believed in friendship. In love. In eternity, the eternity that Amy Harmon gifted with this little blessing, this beautiful and ugly book. I cannot thank you enough, Amy Harmon.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Victory is in the battle.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/8-kat-reviews/571-makingfaces" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more at <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a>!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4541828158937239353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1785721584?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibi" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi">Bibi</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33411728-bibi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785721584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2082562719026588761"><blockquote><b>If I could give this 10 stars, I would. How do I explain the emotions that this book evoked? Dear Lord.</b><br/><br/>Reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces' title='Making Faces by Amy Harmon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Making Faces</a> felt as if I was in a movie theatre, one that had a three sixty degree high definition screen, where each character was portrayed in bold and vivid colours. I felt the pain, joy, sadness, victory, serenity; emotions that were pulled almost effortlessly. <br/><br/>It's difficult to write a review that could even remotely explain how this story decimated my heart.<br/><br/>From Fern to Ambrose t</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2082562719026588761" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>If I could give this 10 stars, I would. How do I explain the emotions that this book evoked? Dear Lord.</b><br /><br />Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces" title="Making Faces by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a> felt as if I was in a movie theatre, one that had a three sixty degree high definition screen, where each character was portrayed in bold and vivid colours. I felt the pain, joy, sadness, victory, serenity; emotions that were pulled almost effortlessly. <br /><br />It's difficult to write a review that could even remotely explain how this story decimated my heart.<br /><br />From Fern to Ambrose to Bailey, Rita, the Sheens, Paulie, Jesse, Bean, Grant, et al. Each character was depicted with such depth, such heart, such love. A love that also brought much pain and changed lives completely. I ached for Fern yet I loved how fearless and selfless she was. Such a beautiful soul. <br /><br />Then there was Ambrose, our male protagonist, whom I loved because Fern loved him and when his life tragically altered, I broke and wept for him. <br /><br /><b>Ms Harmon adroitly mixed profound sadness with enough levity, weaving a balance many authors fail to achieve. This is going on my list of favourites, absolutely.</b></blockquote></span>

  <span id="freeText6925465075951154373" style="display:none">This isn’t just a military book,<br><br>this isn’t just a romance book,<br> <br>this isn’t just a new adult book, <br> <br>For me, this is <b>“the book”</b> of 2013! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492069164ra/22478329.gif" width="400" height="475" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>”Victory is in the battle.”</b>
</i><br><br>Amy Harmon hit it out of the park with this story. The writing is <b>PHENOMENAL</b> the storyline <b>UNIQUE</b> and the characters <b>UNFORGETTABLE</b>!!<br><br>This story is brilliantly told in a narrative format of Fern, Baily, Rita, Ambrose and the friends and families of Hannah Lakes, PA.<br><br>The writing had me continuously highlighting quote after quote. The story brought smiles and tears and I dare a reader not to <b>FEEL</b> when they read this story. <br><br>I just loved the depth of the author’s writing, the feelings, the friendships. I could go on and on but simply put..<br><br><b>
  <i>”Terrible things happen to everyone. Brosey. We’re all just so caught up in our own crap that we don’t see the shit everyone else is wading through.”</i>
</b><br><br>It was absolutely beautiful!<br> <br><b>
  <i>"But maybe you see me because your beautiful, not because I am."</i>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382387946i/5861865._SX540_.jpg" width="401" height="475" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story is so much more than it's description and the characters are the type that stay will you forever.<br><br><b>
  <i>"Everbody is a main character to somebody."</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_1171613454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171613454" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1171613454?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/22912995-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carol [Goodreads Addict] by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4605685-kelly">Kelly</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1171613454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11431887789050146665">Making Faces is the first book I have read by Amy Harmon. Even though I knew what it was going to be about, I wasn’t prepared for the beauty of the words. I wasn’t prepared for the impact the words would have on me. And I wasn’t prepared for the raw emotions this book would make me feel. <br/><br/><a href='http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/477196_zps14qltjxk.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425174392i/13857293.jpg' alt=' photo 477196_zps14qltjxk.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><br/>Fern Taylor is a red headed waif like girl that maybe took a little longer than some to blossom. She had curly crazy red hair, was small and wore braces until her senior year in high school. Her father is a</span>
  <span id="freeText11431887789050146665" style="display:none">Making Faces is the first book I have read by Amy Harmon. Even though I knew what it was going to be about, I wasn’t prepared for the beauty of the words. I wasn’t prepared for the impact the words would have on me. And I wasn’t prepared for the raw emotions this book would make me feel. <br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/477196_zps14qltjxk.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425174392i/13857293.jpg" alt=" photo 477196_zps14qltjxk.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Fern Taylor is a red headed waif like girl that maybe took a little longer than some to blossom. She had curly crazy red hair, was small and wore braces until her senior year in high school. Her father is a pastor and her best friend is her cousin, Bailey, that lives next door. Bailey suffers from muscular dystrophy and is bound to a wheel chair. Fern has learned about love, passion and romance from her addiction to romance novels. Fern is an aspiring romance novel writer. Even though Fern has never had a boyfriend, she has been in love. She has loved Ambrose Young since she was ten years old. <br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/Wrestling_glenninvite020_zpseoex3ocj.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425174392i/13857294._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo Wrestling_glenninvite020_zpseoex3ocj.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Where Fern was tiny, Ambrose was big. He was always large for his age, and strong. He learned early that he had a natural talent for wrestling. He soon became the town wrestling star but along with that came the responsibility not to let his town down. He was always expected to win. Ambrose was also beautiful. His face was beautiful, and Fern loved him. But someone like Ambrose would never notice someone like Fern. <br><br>In their senior year, the year was 2001, and on September 11, their world was changed. Ambrose felt like he wanted to forge his own path, be his own man. So he convinced his four best friends to come along with him and they enlisted. And as so many of the young men who went off to war to defend our country, four of those young men did not come home. But Ambrose did. Except the Ambrose that came home was not the same man that left. His face was badly disfigured. But the changes were more than what you could see on the outside.<br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/humvee%20us%20soldier_zpsbkwq15sh.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425174392i/13857295.jpg" alt=" photo humvee us soldier_zpsbkwq15sh.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ambrose did notice Fern back in high school and she stayed on his mind all the years after he left. But now, he can’t stand for her to see him like this. Fern doesn’t see his scars though. She sees the beauty of Ambrose’s poetic heart. But can she break through the protective walls Ambrose has built around him? Can she convince him that the scars don’t matter?<br><br><b>
  <i>“News flash, Fern Taylor! Everything has changed! You are beautiful, I am hideous, you don’t need me anymore, but I sure as hell need you!”<br><br>“You can have your pride and sit here and make cupcakes and get old and fat and nobody will give a damn after a while. Or you can trade that pride in for a little humility and take your life back.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/tumblr_m4exyuKdhB1ru64uao1_r1_500_zpsinxsqxxv.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425174392i/13857296.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_m4exyuKdhB1ru64uao1_r1_500_zpsinxsqxxv.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was such a beautiful and heart breaking book. It was a story of three people, Fern, Ambrose and Bailey. Bailey, in his wheel chair, was perhaps the strongest of them all with his eyes that missed nothing. He had the courage of a lion. Ambrose who was big, strong, athletic, a natural leader. But he had a poetic heart, a love of Shakespeare, of beautiful words. And Fern, little Fern with the biggest heart of all, who sees something in Ambrose that perhaps Ambrose didn’t even understand. <br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/wheelchairgeneric_zpsamq0fzlp.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425174392i/13857297._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo wheelchairgeneric_zpsamq0fzlp.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ambrose doesn’t feel worthy of Fern’s love. She could have any man. Why would she want him with his scarred face and scarred heart? <br><br><b>
  <i>“No, Fern. I’m not ashamed to be seen with you. I’m ashamed to be seen.”</i>
</b><br><br>But slowly, Fern and Bailey together break through Ambrose’s walls and he opens to them, slowly regaining his self confidence, re-entering society. <br><br><b>
  <i>“She was right. He was partially blind, but in spite of that, maybe because of that, he was seeing things more clearly than he ever had before.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/36202_20130320_100013_Cute-Love-Quotes-For-Him-9-660x503_zpsotame0tj.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425174392i/13857298.png" alt=" photo 36202_20130320_100013_Cute-Love-Quotes-For-Him-9-660x503_zpsotame0tj.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Their happiness is short lived, as tragedy enters their lives once more. Will this bring them closer together or tear apart the tentative bonds they have built? This book will make you smile, break your heart, and put it back together again. The words are so beautiful, the quotes breathtaking. It is my first Amy Harmon book but will not be my last. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11431887789050146665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Amy | Foxy Blogs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs"><img alt="Amy | Foxy Blogs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366176904p2/9955253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/720682523?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy | Foxy Blogs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy | Foxy Blogs" href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs">Amy | Foxy Blogs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=fall-2013-5-stars">fall-2013-5-stars</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=2013-books-i-ve-read">2013-books-i-ve-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer720682523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14395928864194666435"><b>** AUDIO PRICE DROP **<br/>$2.99 (normally $30.00) ➜<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/1agiVPT'>http://amzn.to/1agiVPT</a> <br/></b>4/10/2015<br/>*******************************************************<br/><br/><b>Re-Read</b> (8/5/2015)<br/>I actually listened to this one on a couple family car trips. Even though it's been two years since I originally read it I still experienced all the same feels. <br/>My teens verdict -> they loved it. Thumbs up all around. <br/><br/>*******************************************************<br/><b>P.R.I.C.E.L.E.S.S.</b> <br/>I feel inadequate to write a review that will do this st</span>
  <span id="freeText14395928864194666435" style="display:none"><b>** AUDIO PRICE DROP **<br />$2.99 (normally $30.00) ➜<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1agiVPT">http://amzn.to/1agiVPT</a> <br /></b>4/10/2015<br />*******************************************************<br /><br /><b>Re-Read</b> (8/5/2015)<br />I actually listened to this one on a couple family car trips. Even though it's been two years since I originally read it I still experienced all the same feels. <br />My teens verdict -&gt; they loved it. Thumbs up all around. <br /><br />*******************************************************<br /><b>P.R.I.C.E.L.E.S.S.</b> <br />I feel inadequate to write a review that will do this story the justice it deserves. <br /><br /><b>Absolutely my favorite book of the year! </b>I deliberately read <u>Making Faces</u> slowly to make it last as long as possible. Being immersed in the beauty of this story allowed me to go from laughing to crying to giggling and back to bawling my eyes out. It's a rare find when a book can make you <b>FEEL.</b><br /><br />Reading Making Faces reminded me of how I felt when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16158740.Painted_Faces__Painted_Faces___1_" title="Painted Faces (Painted Faces, #1) by L.H. Cosway" rel="nofollow noopener">Painted Faces</a>. It evoked all the insecurities I have about the question,<i> "Could I be with someone who didn't fit the mold of what society considers 'normal'?</i>" Am I strong enough like Fern and Freda to love men who aren't physically perfect?<br /><blockquote><b><i>"God has given you one face and you make yourself another."</i></b>-Hamlet</blockquote> Can society stop seeing the exterior and see the interior of a person?<blockquote><i>"When you really look at them, you stop seeing a perfect nose or straight teeth. You stop seeing the acne scar or the dimple in the chin. <b> Those things start to blur, and suddenly you see them, the colors, the life inside the shell, and beauty takes on a whole new meaning.</b>"</i> </blockquote><br />Three main characters graced the pages of this book each one equally important.<blockquote><b><i>"Everybody is a main character to someone."</i></b> -Bailey</blockquote><br /><b>Fern</b> has become one of my favorite heroines. The other day a friend asked me if I could be any female book character who would I be...I would be Fern. I loved her grace and passion and her ability to love unconditionally. <br /><br /><b>Bailey</b> is going down as one of my all time favorite characters. His ability to make me laugh and cry has not been out done by any other character yet.<br /><br /><b>Ambrose</b> has so much deep beauty that you can't help but love him. His strength and sense of duty is unmatched. <br /><br />I'm going to be thinking about this story for a long time. When I saw that Amy Harmon had a new book coming out I quickly recommended it to my friends. I knew Ms. Harmon wouldn't disappoint. This story is one I will continue to encourage my friends to read. I know I will read it again. After my husband gave me a funny look for laughing like a crazy person (Bailey had just announced, <i>"You gonna tell me I can't have my seeing-eye cat with me?"</i>) I decided I'm going to read this book to him like I did <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15505346.On_the_Island__On_the_Island___1_" title="On the Island (On the Island, #1) by Tracey Garvis-Graves" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Island</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16056408.Easy__Contours_of_the_Heart___1_" title="Easy (Contours of the Heart, #1) by Tammara Webber" rel="nofollow noopener">Easy</a>. <b>I, for one, am a better person for reading it.</b><br /><br />**Pre-review Personal note from the author** <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><b>FROM THE AUTHOR:</b><br /><br /><u>This One is Personal</u><br />My son, Samuel, was born with a port-wine stain that covered half of his face. It was very dark red and the skin on that side is slightly thicker than the skin on the other side of his face. Luckily for Sam, they can now treat this condition, where even ten-fifteen years ago, that option did not exist. The treatments are very expensive and painful, and so far, Sam has had four laser surgeries, which have improved the overall appearance. He will have to have several more. However, he still gets stares and whispers, and I can't tell you how many times I've overheard someone say, (mostly little kids who don't know better) "What's wrong with his face?"<br /><br />In my new book, Making Faces, I introduce you to Ambrose Young, a handsome, young, athlete who volunteers to serve his country and is injured in Iraq. This is a special story, and it's an important one. It's funny and romantic and heart-breaking. I hope my romance readers won't be turned off by Ambrose Young or his injuries, both emotional and physical. <br /><br />Available on October 20! You can pre-order it on Amazon right now! I would really love to see this book do well, because it isn't your typical romance. It will break your heart, but you'll love every second of it.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Standalone</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_challenges/549008" rel="nofollow noopener">175th book of 2013</a></span>
