    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_738612499" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/738612499" />
    <a title="La-Lionne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11644154-la-lionne"><img alt="La-Lionne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458815714p2/11644154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/738612499?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="La-Lionne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="La-Lionne" href="/user/show/11644154-la-lionne">La-Lionne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=sweet">sweet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=reviews-say-yay-i-say-nay">reviews-say-yay-i-say-nay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=just-blah">just-blah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11644154-la-lionne?shelf=young-love">young-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer738612499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11829540951582073181"><b>***2.8 stars***<br/><u>- WARNING, VERY UNPOPULAR OPINION -</u></b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400613ra/776621.gif' width='330' height='280' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'll <i>try</i> to make it short.<br/>This book didn't work for me for few reasons, and to be honest, I think I'm being too generous giving 2.8, but I loved Bailey that much.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Fern:</u>
</b><br/>There was no debt to her character and no growth. From the flashbacks from her childhood to present day, she stayed the same mellow character throughout the whole book. At first, I though she was cute and sweet, but after couple of hundred pages of reading the same thing over an</span>
  <span id="freeText11829540951582073181" style="display:none"><b>***2.8 stars***<br><u>- WARNING, VERY UNPOPULAR OPINION -</u></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400613ra/776621.gif" width="330" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'll <i>try</i> to make it short.<br>This book didn't work for me for few reasons, and to be honest, I think I'm being too generous giving 2.8, but I loved Bailey that much.<br><br><b>
  <u>Fern:</u>
</b><br>There was no debt to her character and no growth. From the flashbacks from her childhood to present day, she stayed the same mellow character throughout the whole book. At first, I though she was cute and sweet, but after couple of hundred pages of reading the same thing over and over, I got bored. She was a character that could do or say no wrong, one of those characters that rides unicorns and farts rainbows. <br>I didn't buy her being ugly. Quite frankly, If I was a readhead, I would have felt insulted by this book. She was ugly as a kid because she had read hair, freckles and bad teeth, when she was little. Are you f-ing kidding me? You show me a kid age 5 to 10, who's teeth look nice. And braces? How ugly did those look? She wasn't born in the 60's! When kids at that age start loosing their milk teeth, they all look weird-ish, like miniature zombies :). But that doesn't make them ugly. <br>And seriously, since when is red hair and freckles ugly? According to my dictionary ugly means: unpleasant or repulsive, unattractive, ill-favoured, hideous. That part pissed me off a bit. How ugly could she have been if she managed to grow into a beautiful 'swan', a hot chick that everyone oohed and aahed when they saw her?<br>Then, she was giving Ambrose pep-talks about knowing how he felt, being insecure about his looks, because she went through the same thing. Like he will grow out of it or something. Give me a break.<br><br><b>
  <u>Ambrose:</u>
</b><br>At the beginning I liked him a lot. That scene where teacher came into his classroom and turned the TV on was absolutely heartbreaking. I admired him for wanting to join the army. His reasons were very heroic. But, and it's huge one, I didn't like how he convinced his friends to join the army. That particular scene where he tried to talk his friends into coming with him made me sooo mad. Especially when later <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his friends died in Iraq. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I understand he was young and there was a lot of things he didn't know about what it's like to fight in a war, but he did signed up for the right reason. What got me all worked up was how he convinced his friends to join him. I would have loved for him to have told them the reasons why he signed up, maybe take more patriotic approach in trying to convince them. He thought it would be fun to hang out with the guys, and that Iraq was the place to do it!!! You must be freaking kidding! They all were "Sure, why not, I have nothing better to do, and chicks dig solders, so let's do it" Like they were talking about some fun camping trip. <br>In the parts where they were in Iraq, all they did were talk about girls. I never got the feeling that they were actually fighting in a war, up until the last scene in Iraq where road-side bomb exploded. And even that was a very short scene. <br>I did sympathized with Ambrose for what he was going through later, I just wished that some of the parts with his recovery were explored more. After a while it felt like his main concern was the fact that he looked ugly. Author barely scratched the surface of PTSD. I kept wishing to read more about his recovery and how he came to terms with what happened, but all I got was more quotes from Hamlet and Shakespeare and passages from the Bible. And endless talk about wrestling. Don't even get me started on that. If I never hear word 'wrestling' again, it will be too soon.<br><br><b>
  <u>A&amp;F together:</u>
</b><br>Fern was in love with Ambrose long before the book started. She loved him this vanilla-baby-love. She always looked at him with those big puppy-eyes. And it was fine, when she was younger, but when she got older, that little girl crush just felt weird.<br>Throughout the book it was said, numerous times, that Ambrose never thought that Fern was ugly. But he never approached her, never asked her on a date, or to a dance. He was chasing a school slut's, Rita's tail. <br>They were adults when they finally got together, but their love felt so juvenile and teenage-like. Yes, there were couple of cute moments, like the kiss in the park, but it wasn't enough to connect me to them. And I don't mean that I wanted explicit sex scenes. I wanted for their love to grow and develop, to turn into something profound and bigger than life. Their constant quoting of Hamlet and Shakespeare wasn't doing it for me.<br><br><b>
  <u>Bailey:</u>
</b><br>Now him, I loved. Such a sweetheart. I could not get enough of his character. I think I marked almost everything he said. Such wonderful and smart kid. His story was heartbreaking. That little, weak body had such an enormous soul. He was the voice of reason. And a nice break from those two whiners "me, me me, boohoo, I'm ugly, my life is over". And I'm not trying to make fun of either F or A for what they went through, I just felt like those two were way too self-centered, and I liked that he pointed that out. And that scene where he asked Rita to dance was so precious. His character gets 5 easiest stars I have ever given.<br><blockquote>* * *</blockquote>I remember reading a review where it was said that just because characters can quote Hamlet and Shakespeare doesn't mean they are deep. I completely agree. There was quote, upon quote, upon quote. Sometime, after I passed 50% mark, I remember rolling my eyes every time I read name Hamlet or Shakespeare. The quotes were beautiful and somewhat romantic, but there were sooo many of them. I wished they would have stopped quoting someone else and would have come up with something interesting and original, something of their own, to say. If I wanted to know what Hamlet's or Shakespeare's opinions were on this or that subject, I would have gone and read their work. I thought author overdid with quotes.<br><br>Then we have God and Jesus. Before I say anything else, I want to say that I understand that when 9/11 happened a lot of people turned to God. Some to look for answers, others to blame Him for what happened. Because nothing seemed fair. It still doesn't. <br>This book has a very strong christian theme, and I wished it was mentioned in the blurb. And after I read the book, I thought that the cover didn't make much sense. <br>Constant quoting from the Bible was just too much for me. I felt like author was trying shove God and Jesus down my throat. He said this and he did that. And to top it all of, her father's favorite t-shirt had the writing "what would Jesus do" on it. I mean... pfff... Seriously? I get it, he's a pastor, but come on. <br><br>Then there was the Rita-character. She spend most of the book f*cking around, and then suddenly, at the end, I read "I always had feeling for Bailey." Whoa..t? Spare me the bull! I did feel bad for what she went through later in the story, but I still didn't like her. I didn't wish her ill, but she didn't deserve Bailey, he was too good for her. And I didn't buy her having romantic feeling for him.<br><br>So there you have it, my thoughts on this book. So much for my review being short :).<br><br>---------------------------------------------------------------<br>BR with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11057966-alex" rel="nofollow noopener">Alex</a> aka Image Ruiner :-D <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383060847ra/6366704.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11829540951582073181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/736747176" />
    <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie"><img alt="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505392311p2/11641363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/736747176?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie">Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=give-this-author-a-bells">give-this-author-a-bells</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer736747176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6594886671471007129"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382276445i/5784425.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Going in to this book, I thought I new what to expect. I new it had a military theme because I'd read the blurb and I thought I new what was going to happen. <br/><br/>So imagine my surprise when I read it and discovered that it wasn't at all about what I expected. This is Fern and Ambrose's story, but it's about so much more than that. It's a story about loss, pain and self acceptance.<br/><br/>Making Faces sends a messages to the reader. For me the one word that came to mind is <b>Perception.</b> We all have our own per</span>
  <span id="freeText6594886671471007129" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382276445i/5784425.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Going in to this book, I thought I new what to expect. I new it had a military theme because I'd read the blurb and I thought I new what was going to happen. <br><br>So imagine my surprise when I read it and discovered that it wasn't at all about what I expected. This is Fern and Ambrose's story, but it's about so much more than that. It's a story about loss, pain and self acceptance.<br><br>Making Faces sends a messages to the reader. For me the one word that came to mind is <b>Perception.</b> We all have our own perceptions, when you look at someone how does your perception of them differ from someone else. What constitutes beauty and is our understanding of it flawed.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382276445i/5784426.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ambrose, is the town's pride. He's handsome, athletic, he has the perfect life. At least on the outside that's how it seems, until one day an event that changed the world forced him to look at his own life differently. <br><br>So five friends just out of high school go off to war but their time is cut short when and Ambrose comes back by alone. Broken and filled with guilt he lives inside of himself, until a girl he never paid much attention to forces him out of the shell he's built around himself.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382276445i/5784427.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fern, an extraordinary soul that came in an ordinary package. She's loved Ambrose for as long as she can remember. When he left he took a little bit of her heart with him, so when he comes back she's elated and filled with guilt at the same time. <br><br>Fern has <b>"ugly girl syndrome"</b>, she doesn't see the beauty she has, both inside and outside. But as she and Ambrose slowly begin to discover each others secrets, she slowly comes out of her own shell.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382276445i/5784428.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book touched my heart, I honestly have no clue what else to say besides <b>READ THIS BOOK</b> I cried so much, but it was bittersweet, I was heart broken I was over joyed. This isn't one of those books where death or disease is used as trigger for the reader, the author doesn't force you to feel a certain way. The story tells itself and because of that you feel a part of it.<br><br>This book will leave you with an egg sized blob of emotion in your throat, it's really beautiful. I'm sitting here writing this review trying to find something I didn't love about it and I can't. I love to feel and this book allowed me too.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382276660i/5784653.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>ARC kindly provided by author and appreciated by me :)</i></span>

<div id="review_1471432620" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471432620" />
    <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna"><img alt="✦❋Arianna✦❋" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420671997p2/23370948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1471432620?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471432620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3697928083657539419"><b>5 Stars!!</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450793680i/17470215.jpg' width='400' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>“Making Faces"</i> was hands down the most emotional book I have read by this author. Once again Amy Harmon bewitched me with her beautiful story, captivating flawless writing and her fantastic storytelling. I was so hooked from the beginning that I couldn’t put it down. This book was everything I was expected and everything I wanted. <i>“Making Faces”</i> is a touching, though-provoking, beautifully written story about life, love, family, self-acceptance and friendship. Is a story about what it </span>
  <span id="freeText3697928083657539419" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars!!</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450793680i/17470215.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“Making Faces"</i> was hands down the most emotional book I have read by this author. Once again Amy Harmon bewitched me with her beautiful story, captivating flawless writing and her fantastic storytelling. I was so hooked from the beginning that I couldn’t put it down. This book was everything I was expected and everything I wanted. <i>“Making Faces”</i> is a touching, though-provoking, beautifully written story about life, love, family, self-acceptance and friendship. Is a story about what it means to be a hero, about courage, war and loss. Is a story about what true beauty really means. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If God made all out faces, did he laugh when he made me?” - Fern</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Fern has red hair, freckles, braces and glasses. She’s a little odd and she loves to read. She’s smart, sweet and she loves to care for her cousin and best friend, Bailey who’s in a wheelchair and has Dushenne muscular dystrophy. She believes she has forgettable features and that she is that kind of girl who’s easily overlooked and ignored. She 's sure the boy who had loved since she was ten years old will never notice her.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“To Fern, Ambrose Young was absolutely beautiful, a Greek God among mortals, the stuff of fairy tales and movie screens.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Ambrose is the opposite of Fern in every single way. He’s handsome, popular and a the star wrestler of the town. Unfortunately, he doesn’t know Fern exists. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450793680i/17470216.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Could you belong to someone who didn’t want you? Fern decided it was possible because her heart was his, and whether or not he wanted it didn’t seem to make much difference.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Some events make Ambrose open his eyes and he eventually finds out Fern is special, different from any other girl he met. He’s not ready for college and since he always dreamed of being a different kind of hero, dreamed of being a soldier, he enlists in the army, persuading his four closest friends to come along with him.<br><br>Three years later, Fern still lives in the small town. While not many things had changed in her life, Ambrose’s life changed irrevocably during his service. He’s damaged in more ways than one, scarred inside and out and he’s ready to give up on life than to start over. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448713154ra/17179734.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What scares you the most, son?” his father asked quietly.<br> <br>Ambrose wanted to laugh. He wasn't afraid of anything. Not anymore. “Not a damn thing, Dad. I used to be afraid of going to hell. But now that I'm here, hell doesn't seem so bad.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Ambrose is changed and suffers from PTSD. There are days when the guilt he feels is too much for him. Fern never forget Ambrose. She never stopped loving him and now all she wants is to help the boy who always had her heart.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434724161i/15256274.jpg" width="400" height="90" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This was such a compelling, emotional read! I absolutely loved the storytelling which was quite different from the author’s other books. This book made me feel so much! It was equally heartbreaking and heartwarming and deeply moving from the start. It was refreshing, unique and it made me smile and grin and cry.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You read smutty romance novels and quote scripture. I'm not quite sure I have you figured out.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Fern is a heroine you will fell in love with from the beginning. She's a heroine you will want to be friend with, a heroine that will make you feel and think about life, family and friendship and maybe a heroine you will connect with. She was such an endearing character and her character’s development was pure and simple stellar. She is genuinely a good person, with a heart of gold. She’s sweet, caring, protective, thoughtful and honestly she’s one of the greatest heroine I had the pleasure to read about. Seeing her come out of her invisible shell was heart-warming. Her “transformation” was in some way satisfying, believable and overall really well done. She had all my admiration for sacrificing her future to be with her cousin, Bailey and later for being persistent in showing Ambrose that people who cared about him still care, despite the fact his appearance changed. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“…maybe her love would simply loosen the strings, freeing him to walk away.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450793680ra/17470217.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ambrose is a hero in every possible way. His journey broke my heart. You can feel at times how lost and lonely he his, his despair, his guilt, how much he struggles to accept his new reality. He is kind and sweet and a great friend for both Bailey and Fern. <br><br>A character I absolutely loved is Bailey. Bailey melt my heart. He made me smile more times than I can count. He was such a sweet soul and he truly felt like breath of fresh air. He was sweet and so protective with Fern and such a great friend for both his cousin and Ambrose. I loved his strength, his honesty and also his determination to live his life at the fullest despite the fact he was so sick. I loved his connection with Fern and I adored their closeness.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450793680i/17470218.jpg" width="400" height="393" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fern and Ambrose’s relationship unfolded slow, but sure. Their bond was powerful, real and I simply loved it. They were so good for each other and their connection was really beautiful. They gave each other everything and I loved how they became more. <br><br>All in all, <i>“Making Faces”</i> was a wonderful, moving tale with a powerful message that I loved – beauty comes from the inside – characters that will touch you deeply and a story line that will give you many life lessons. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Maybe everyone represents a piece of the puzzle. We all fit together to create this experience we call life. None of us can see the part we play or the way it all turns out. Maybe the miracles that we see are just the tip of the iceberg. And maybe we just don't recognize the blessings that come as a result of terrible things.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434724161i/15256274.jpg" width="400" height="90" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>**Highly recommended!**</u>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3697928083657539419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666133058?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666133058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6184981582405912517"><b>(More than) 5 Stars!!!</b><br/><br/>Talk about an amazing book at its most extreme! <b>This book is a rare gem</b>. You know it's crafted to tear your heart into a million pieces but you still read it anyways 'coz it's beautifully written and heartfelt!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443470366ra/16363719.gif' width='350' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Maybe everyone represents a piece of the puzzle. We all fit together to create this experience we call life. None of us can see the part we play or the way we see are just the tip of the iceberg. And maybe we just don't recognize the blessings that come as a </b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6184981582405912517" style="display:none"><b>(More than) 5 Stars!!!</b><br><br>Talk about an amazing book at its most extreme! <b>This book is a rare gem</b>. You know it's crafted to tear your heart into a million pieces but you still read it anyways 'coz it's beautifully written and heartfelt!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443470366ra/16363719.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Maybe everyone represents a piece of the puzzle. We all fit together to create this experience we call life. None of us can see the part we play or the way we see are just the tip of the iceberg. And maybe we just don't recognize the blessings that come as a result of terrible things."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces" title="Making Faces by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a> is a story about a girl named <b>Fern Taylor</b>. She's one of those protagonists people call an 'ugly duckling' because of her frizzy wild red hair, crooked teeth, a million freckles on her face, and huge eyeglasses. But even though she grew up with a knowledge that she's not physically attractive like the rest of the girls in <i>Hannah Lake</i>, she was well-loved by her parents and her cousin and best friend <b>Bailey</b>. While in high school, she developed this infatuation to <b>Ambrose Young</b>, Hannah Lake's golden boy and the most popular guy and most looked-up to. Ambrose has all the things young girls will fall in love with. He's beautiful, strong, smart, talented, athletic, perfect. But when 9/11 happened in the U.S. which urged him to sign up for military together with his close friends, his life changed and he returned home with a tortured soul and a ruined physicality.<br><br><b>I can't believe I haven't read it sooner.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a> is such a genius and a talented author and I knew it just by reading the first few paragraphs of the book. She did a wonderful job in this novel because of the way she chose words that absolutely hit home. All throughout the book I found myself hanging on to every word because I'm afraid I'll be missing out a tiny detail. <br><br>What struck me most about this book was how the author inspired everything based on <b>real life</b>. The characters she featured were so raw and without any pretense. The main setting she chose was also peaceful and quiet and in a way, very comforting. I also loved the fact that the book tackled some <b>inspiring and religious concepts</b> which made me ponder my own reality. It also gave us the glimpse about the experiences military men face outside the country and what it would be like to work in those areas away from home and from loved ones.<br><br>I cried a lot of times all throughout the book because of the deep and meaningful messages it instilled and how it portrayed the importance of being close to God as much as being close to your family and friends. I also learned from this book that inner beauty is more important than physical beauty and what matters most is the good things you impact to someone's life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I think sometines a beautiful face is false advertising too, and too many of us don't take the time to look beneath the lid."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The book also has a good romance in it. Ambrose and Fern's romantic development-- from childhood strangers to friends to lovers-- was so remarkable. It developed naturally and beautifully. Their love was so inspiring I don't think I would ever forget it. I am forever thankful that authors like Amy Harmon exist. <b>An incredible book like this deserves the spotlight</b>. It's one that I wouldn't trade for any book. <br><br>In Making Faces, the emotions emanating from the pages and the overall impact was truly worth the ride. So if you're looking for a book that will provide you a good cry, do yourself a favor and put this on top of your tbr! :')<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Thank you for making even ugly things beautiful."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><p>
  <a href="https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446199662i/16763926._SX540_.jpg" alt="Pearl's Book Journey (1)" width="380" height="190" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464648592i/19260109.png" width="250" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_2561007350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2561007350" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2561007350?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781633920958" href="/book/show/30027407-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2561007350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13358019766019738801">what a surprise this book was. the kind of quiet surprise that ever so quietly draws closer to you, step by step, until its staring right back at you, making you realise and say, <i>‘oh, there you are. i didnt know how much i needed you.’</i><br/><br/>this was such a tender love story, as all love stories should be. but where the surprise came from was not the fondness i felt for the romantic and healing love between two people who desperately needed it, but seeing the importance of a strong and resilient love b</span>
  <span id="freeText13358019766019738801" style="display:none">what a surprise this book was. the kind of quiet surprise that ever so quietly draws closer to you, step by step, until its staring right back at you, making you realise and say, <i>‘oh, there you are. i didnt know how much i needed you.’</i><br /><br />this was such a tender love story, as all love stories should be. but where the surprise came from was not the fondness i felt for the romantic and healing love between two people who desperately needed it, but seeing the importance of a strong and resilient love between friends and family. that, to me, was the greatest gift of this book.<br /><br />even though i appreciated the message ambrose and ferns romance represented - the importance of finding beauty in all things, even the ugly - what really moved me was the unwavering bond shared between a group of boys and also the ties between two cousins that transcended familial affection. i think sometimes stories about love tend to focus so much on romantic relationships and forget that other relationships are just as influential, just as noteworthy. i love how this story showed that, and how that love for friends and family also has the power to get you through the devastating loss of those people. <br /><br />if i could change anything about this, it would probably be the way the story was told. i found the constant transitions between the present and past to be a little jarring, especially with the lack of transitions. i think had this been told in a chronological fashion, it would have been much more effective. there were also some events towards the end that felt a little out of place. <br /><br />but overall, this was a beautiful and moving book. i can definitely see why so many praise amy harmon. her writing and stories are definitely ones to pick up! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13358019766019738801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_745817806" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/745817806" />
    <a title="• Lisa •" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11963959-lisa"><img alt="• Lisa •" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576172089p2/11963959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/745817806?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lisa •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lisa •" href="/user/show/11963959-lisa">• Lisa •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to • Lisa • by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11963959-lisa?shelf=my-friend-anna-and-her-weepy-reads">my-friend-anna-and-her-weepy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11963959-lisa?shelf=love-you-forever-and-ever">love-you-forever-and-ever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer745817806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13970381525290264248"><b>5 BEAUTIFUL STARS</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>"And so we endure. We have faith that there is purpose. We have hope for things that we can't see. We believe that there are lessons in loss, power in love ... </b>
</i> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382611780i/6061002._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>
  <b> "... and that we have within us the potential for a beauty so magnificent that our bodies can't contain it."</b>
</i><br/><br/>Well readers I could not resist going straight into this book, everywhere I turned this book was all over my Goodreads feed. So like the dutiful addict I am and with several recommendations thrown my way I</span>
  <span id="freeText13970381525290264248" style="display:none"><b>5 BEAUTIFUL STARS</b><br><br><i>
  <b>"And so we endure. We have faith that there is purpose. We have hope for things that we can't see. We believe that there are lessons in loss, power in love ... </b>
</i> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382611780i/6061002._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b> "... and that we have within us the potential for a beauty so magnificent that our bodies can't contain it."</b>
</i><br><br>Well readers I could not resist going straight into this book, everywhere I turned this book was all over my Goodreads feed. So like the dutiful addict I am and with several recommendations thrown my way I picked up my kindle, the obligatory handful of tissues and prepared my book heart for a good old weepy work out, and it was worth every single tissue and every heartfelt five stars. Here are my 'Making faces' thoughts ...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382611780i/6061003._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What's it all about?</b><br>Please go into this book with an open heart and I guarantee you will be changed. I haven't got the words to sum up what this beautiful story is about. But I will say that this book is a story of love, life, tragedy and finding the beauty inside those we meet in our lives. There's a lesson to be learned from this book, go be taught.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382611780i/6061004._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What did I love?</b><br>The book is not over dramatic in its presentation it tugs at the heart strings in all the right ways, I applaud the author for tackling such sensitive and tragic subjects in a way which was realistic and heart felt, I never felt emotionally black mailed by this story but I was gripped by every page and turn of events. It felt like the author had a personal story to tell and she delivered it with sensitivity and heart. The friendships in this book were the glue to this story for me, this author obviously has hands on experience of what it is like to have honest to goodness love in your life. I was touched to the core with the way she described the relationships in this book. The characters all had their own spot light and even though there was lots to be told by this story it always flowed well and the writing style was nothing short of poetic. The characters were out of this world. I loved the heroine and hero in equal measure and in actuality the book delivered two heroes; Ambrose Young and Bailey, These two strong loveable characters filled my reading time with delight and heartache I could not have anticipated how these fictional characters could find a place in my heart so easily. I was floored at the authors ability to bring both their lives into the limelight and weave a blend of tragic and endearing into the pages. Every book needs a dutiful heroine and this author delivered to her readers, Fern Taylor what a sweet, unassuming, wonderfully put together character, Fern is a readers dream, her selfless action and larger than life heart leapt out from each page. These characters were lovingly created by an author who obviously spend time and effort drawing together a story that it's wonderfully beautiful. I'm not convinced I have words to express all the things I loved about this story one things for sure it's going to stay with me for some time to come.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382611780i/6061005._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Rating further explored ...</b><br>As well written and put together this story is, it was blanketed with a melancholy and tragic feel to it and whilst I appreciated that the author was setting the tone for a heartbreaking tale it dampened the enjoyment factor somewhat for my reading experience. This book is clearly a five star diamond but aspects of this tragic story shook my reading time. But make no mistake this rating comes with a recommendation and a feeling that I will never forget this original story and consequently the author.There were times throughout this book that I battled with my rating sometimes it felt five star, sometimes it felt less there were times of devastation and times of elation but there is one thing that remained there are some stories that need to be told - making faces is one of them, this story will stay in my book heart for time to come and that is why it can't be anything but a soul changing five stars.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382612143i/6061393._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Final thoughts ...</b><br>Making faces is a book that demands to be experienced not explained, so with that thought in mind if you don't mind a story that will squeeze your heart to its end and fill you with hope and love then I have nothing else to say but go grab it readers, enjoy ... Kisses.</span>

<div id="review_1655331586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655331586" />
    <a title="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog"><img alt="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484605631p2/44673856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655331586?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" href="/user/show/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog">Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655331586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer283495241748505933"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463878552i/19170476.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465414552i/19353177._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>➦This is definitely a book that makes you feel and think about things like your <b>own mortality, standards of beauty and dealing with the loss of loved ones.</b> It's not just a love a story, it's a story that will have you experience emotions while you go through the journey with the characters. <br/><br/>➦<b>Fern</b> is a girl who experiences an <b>"ugly girl syndrome."</b> She in not particularly pretty and she is awkward. That, however, does not stop her from loving <b>Ambrose</b>, a beautiful boy and a wrestler at her high sch</span>
  <span id="freeText283495241748505933" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463878552i/19170476.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465414552i/19353177._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>➦This is definitely a book that makes you feel and think about things like your <b>own mortality, standards of beauty and dealing with the loss of loved ones.</b> It's not just a love a story, it's a story that will have you experience emotions while you go through the journey with the characters. <br><br>➦<b>Fern</b> is a girl who experiences an <b>"ugly girl syndrome."</b> She in not particularly pretty and she is awkward. That, however, does not stop her from loving <b>Ambrose</b>, a beautiful boy and a wrestler at her high school. <b>She knows that someone as beautiful as him would never be with someone like her.</b> <br><br>➦The main characters get <b>re-united</b> years later after Ambrose comes back from Iraq with <b>half of his face disfigured.</b> He survives, while four of his best friends do not. Ambrose struggles to find a way to live with his guilt and his new image. And here begins the journey of Fern and Ambrose, where they <b>help each other heal</b> and fall in love. It's beautiful, really.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465414552i/19353176._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➦In this novel there is also a <b>story of a boy who is wheelchair bound</b> because of a disease. It's a boy who is Fern's best friend and who she cares for throughout his life. It's a heartbreaking story of someone who accepts that his days are numbered but stays positive despite it and tries to <b>experience as many things as he can until he dies.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465414552i/19353178._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>❤All the poems and the references to Greek mythology incorporated into the novel were wonderful. I will definitely remember this book for a long time. <b>I loved the characters, the beautiful words and the strong messages they delivered. </b><br><br>➦I could have totally lived without Bible quoting and references to God but they were few and didn't bother me as much. <br><br>➦If you still haven't read this book and you love romantic novels that will make you feel, you should definitely pick this book up. If you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1357108762s/15507958.jpg" alt="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_753474210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/753474210" />
    <a title="Penny Reid" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18630626-penny-reid"><img alt="Penny Reid" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548810992p2/18630626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/753474210?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny Reid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny Reid" href="/user/show/18630626-penny-reid">Penny Reid</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18630626-penny-reid?shelf=indie-authors">indie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18630626-penny-reid?shelf=11-stars">11-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18630626-penny-reid?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer753474210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer211364741813491127">WARNING: Do not read this book while flying on a plane sitting next to a judgy, disapproving man who is giving you no elbow space and who has no Kleenex tissues because:<br/>1) YOU WILL NEED TISSUES<br/>2) YOU WILL NEED SOME SPACE<br/>3) JUDGY, DISAPPROVING MEN SHOULD NOT BE ALLOWED ON PLANES (or in public)<br/><br/>This book was recommended to me by Jenny the Book Sojourner (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://booksojourner.blogspot.com/'>http://booksojourner.blogspot.com/</a>) and now I have to add her to my Festivus card list and send her a thank you bouquet of flowers. <br/><br/>This.<br/>Book.<br/>Is.<br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText211364741813491127" style="display:none">WARNING: Do not read this book while flying on a plane sitting next to a judgy, disapproving man who is giving you no elbow space and who has no Kleenex tissues because:<br />1) YOU WILL NEED TISSUES<br />2) YOU WILL NEED SOME SPACE<br />3) JUDGY, DISAPPROVING MEN SHOULD NOT BE ALLOWED ON PLANES (or in public)<br /><br />This book was recommended to me by Jenny the Book Sojourner (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://booksojourner.blogspot.com/">http://booksojourner.blogspot.com/</a>) and now I have to add her to my Festivus card list and send her a thank you bouquet of flowers. <br /><br />This.<br />Book.<br />Is.<br />Awesome.<br /><br />But, this book (I feel) is misclassified as a romance. This is actually literary fiction. Yes, there is a romance in the book. But this book is so much more. It is about families, a community, coming of age, relationships, death, sickness, unfulfilled desire, suspense, acceptance, God and faith.<br /><br />Needless to say, Amy Harmon is an outstanding writer. She is a story teller, my favorite kind of author.<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who likes fantastic books. If you don't like fantastic books then maybe this isn't for you.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="211364741813491127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3541105474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3541105474" />
    <a title="Mali Mor ❤️ The Romantic Blogger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88472183-mali-mor-the-romantic-blogger"><img alt="Mali Mor ❤️ The Romantic Blogger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560790165p2/88472183.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3541105474?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mali Mor ❤️ The Romantic Blogger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mali Mor ❤️ The Romantic Blogger" href="/user/show/88472183-mali-mor-the-romantic-blogger">Mali Mor ❤️ The Romantic Blogger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3541105474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer76653259352539084"><a href='https://ibb.co/QHG1HWZ' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599720514ra/30085898.gif' alt='10-09-2020-07-54-37-4750000' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Ambrose Young is a handsome, popular and a talented athlete. He's the kind of guy you see on the covers of romantic novels (according to Fern). Sure, he's beautiful on the outside - but also on the inside, only he doesn't show it... 💥<br/><br/>Fern Taylor knows she's the kind of girl you ignored because of her wild red hair, freckles, crooked teeth and thick glasses - but Fern is an ugly duckling who turns out to be a swan. She's beautiful inside and out. ❤<br/><br/>📚 𝐈𝐟 𝐆𝐨𝐝 𝐦𝐚𝐤𝐞𝐬 𝐚𝐥𝐥 𝐨𝐮𝐫 𝐟𝐚𝐜𝐞𝐬, 𝐝𝐢𝐝 𝐡𝐞 𝐥𝐚𝐮𝐠𝐡 𝐰𝐡</span>
  <span id="freeText76653259352539084" style="display:none"><a href="https://ibb.co/QHG1HWZ" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599720514ra/30085898.gif" alt="10-09-2020-07-54-37-4750000" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ambrose Young is a handsome, popular and a talented athlete. He's the kind of guy you see on the covers of romantic novels (according to Fern). Sure, he's beautiful on the outside - but also on the inside, only he doesn't show it... 💥<br><br>Fern Taylor knows she's the kind of girl you ignored because of her wild red hair, freckles, crooked teeth and thick glasses - but Fern is an ugly duckling who turns out to be a swan. She's beautiful inside and out. ❤<br><br>📚 𝐈𝐟 𝐆𝐨𝐝 𝐦𝐚𝐤𝐞𝐬 𝐚𝐥𝐥 𝐨𝐮𝐫 𝐟𝐚𝐜𝐞𝐬, 𝐝𝐢𝐝 𝐡𝐞 𝐥𝐚𝐮𝐠𝐡 𝐰𝐡𝐞𝐧 𝐡𝐞 𝐦𝐚𝐝𝐞 𝐦𝐞? 📚<br><br>Fern has loved Ambrose since she was 10, but he never saw her. After graduating from high school and even though his future was planned, Ambrose joins the army - but another person returns instead. 💔<br>Ambrose is no longer the god he was and Fern is no longer an ugly duckling, but despite the darkness he lives in, when Fern shines her light on him, he becomes the hero he always wanted to be... Hercules. 💪<br><br>While Fern and Ambrose were the main heroes, Bailey (Fren's cousin) was a hero too. He was the glue of the story and helped them understand that a hero is not only measured by his external power - and beauty is not just what you can see. 💥💥💥<br><br>📚 𝐒𝐨𝐦𝐞𝐭𝐢𝐦𝐞𝐬 𝐰𝐞 𝐟𝐚𝐥𝐥 𝐢𝐧 𝐥𝐨𝐯𝐞 𝐰𝐢𝐭𝐡 𝐚 𝐟𝐚𝐜𝐞 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐧𝐨𝐭 𝐰𝐡𝐚𝐭'𝐬 𝐛𝐞𝐡𝐢𝐧𝐝 𝐢𝐭. 📚<br><br>WOW, what an amazing book! I have no other way to describe it other than a TRUE ROMANCE - full of insights, the kind you can't help but fall in love with. ❤😭<br>It's an emotional story about friendship, courage and unconditional love... But also death, war and trauma.<br><br>The characters crawled into my heart, the plot touched my soul and the writing left me speechless. GO READ IT!!! 👑<br><br>• I listened to the AUDIO version. 🎧 - Rob Shapiro (the Narrator) did an amazing job! He managed to make me feel like I was reading, not hearing it - and thanks to him I was fascinated from start to finish. ❤<br><br>▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️<br><br>📖 ᖴOᒪᒪOᗯ ᗰE Oᑎ IᑎᔕTᗩGᖇᗩᗰ: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/the_romantic_blogger/">https://www.instagram.com/the_romanti...</a><br><br>📖 ᐯIᔕIT ᗰY ᗷᒪOG ᖴOᖇ ᗰOᖇE ᖇEᐯIEᗯᔕ: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://books-romance.com/">https://books-romance.com/</a><br><br>📖 GOOᗪᖇEᗩᗪᔕ: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bit.ly/3acMRMP">https://bit.ly/3acMRMP</a><br><br>💕 לקריאת הסקירה בעברית, כנסו לבלוג: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://books-romance.com/">https://books-romance.com/</a> 💕</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer269792919356698587"><b>5 COMPLETELY AMAZING STARS!!! (And only because I can’t give more than 5.)</b>	<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382605069i/6054181.jpg' width='450' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In a town when everyone knows each other and things don’t remain hidden for very long, Fern is love with Ambrose since she was a little kid and he helped her with a spider’s funeral. Ambrose got to war and when he came back, he was different… he was seen to</span>
  <span id="freeText269792919356698587" style="display:none"><b>5 COMPLETELY AMAZING STARS!!! (And only because I can’t give more than 5.)</b>	<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382605069i/6054181.jpg" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In a town when everyone knows each other and things don’t remain hidden for very long, Fern is love with Ambrose since she was a little kid and he helped her with a spider’s funeral. But Fern never thought that she could be pretty enough for him and so she kept her feelings secret.<br>But then the September 11th came and it changed a small town’s life. Ambrose got to war and when he came back, he was different… he was seen too much dark. <br>And he no longer was the beautiful boy he once was, he has scars… and not only physical ones. <br>And within the dark that he is now… Fern is the one who surprisingly can make him see the light. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382605069i/6054182.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don’t let the simplicity of the plot fool you… this story is utterly amazing and so perfectly written that you’ll never want to leave their world… and that will make you hope for Fern and Ambrose’s love so much as if it was your own. <br>If there are books with such a beautiful story, such amazing characters and that will stay in your heart for a long…LONG time, this is definitely that book. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382605069i/6054183.png" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don’t waste any more time, go read this. </span>

    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1898347474?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=contemporaries">contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=couples-i-love">couples-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way">broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=read-to-review">read-to-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=disability-and-chronic-illness">disability-and-chronic-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1898347474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7746427393014154318"><b>4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Overview:</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “It’s hard to come to terms with the fact that you aren’t ever going to be loved the way you want to be loved.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495943962ra/22869660.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I knew I would love this book. <br/><br/>I don’t know <i>why.</i> This book is so far out of my usual comfort-zone it’s ridiculous. I <i>never</i> read NA. Usually my cynical brain gets bored half-way through a romance. <br/><br/>But somehow I gravitated towards this title, and wished for it on Netgalley late one night. So imagine my surprise when my wish was granted—four years after the publicat</span>
  <span id="freeText7746427393014154318" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars<br><br>Overview:</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote> “It’s hard to come to terms with the fact that you aren’t ever going to be loved the way you want to be loved.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495943962ra/22869660.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I knew I would love this book. <br><br>I don’t know <i>why.</i> This book is so far out of my usual comfort-zone it’s ridiculous. I <i>never</i> read NA. Usually my cynical brain gets bored half-way through a romance. <br><br>But somehow I gravitated towards this title, and wished for it on Netgalley late one night. So imagine my surprise when my wish was granted—four years after the publication date? Thanks to Amy Harmon for the opportunity!<br><br><b>Pros:</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote> “How did you know I needed you?”<br>“Because I needed you.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>If you listen real carefully, I’m pretty sure you can still hear little shards of my heart bouncing on the floor somewhere. <br><br>This feels so <i>genuine.</i> <br>It’s sad. It made me cry <s>(a lot)</s> but it didn’t feel manipulative. It wasn’t some contrived plot I was <i>supposed</i> to feel sad about. <br><br>Every character was developed and interesting, so I FELT for them. <br><br>The writing is just gorgeous. Harmon has a mastery over words and I will definitely be reading more of her books. Overall, it flowed very quickly and I was <i>completely</i> engrossed. I really didn’t want to put this down, and I’ve been thinking about it ever since I finished.<br><br>I went into this very blind. (I didn’t even read all the blurb, tbh) Because of that, I really never knew where the plot was going. I had ideas and suspicious, but the way everything played out was interesting. <br><br>Even the side characters are interesting and feel genuine. Everyone’s family was different and impactful, and I love the way it all came together. <br><br>Fern and Amrbose were beautiful. They woke up my cold-cynical heart and I was <i>so invested.</i> I just wanted them to be happy. Their healing was gradual and precious and I literally don’t know why I loved it so much, but I <i>did.</i> (Even if there were a few points where I thought it might be a bit much, I still loved them.)<br><br><i>
  <blockquote> “Caring about someone doesn’t [always] mean taking care of them.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>^This ^Part ^Killed ^Me<br><br>It’s smart. It’s realistic. It fits her development <i>and</i> his. It’s overall just a really good mentality and not one I <i>ever</i> see.<br><br>I knew this was going to be sad. From the prologue you get an idea and spend half the time preparing yourself. But then it all plays out in a completely different and devastating way.<br><br><b>Cons:</b><br><br>My heart says five stars, but my brain had a few little issues. <br><br>Mainly, that as much as I loved Fern and Ambrose’s relationship, I wanted more focus on Fern herself. It seemed like Amrbose had a fully formed arc, but Fern’s mostly revolved around him. She was a very interesting character, but I wish there’d been more focus on what she plans outside her relationships. Does she want to school? Leave Hannah Lake? Work at the grocery store forever? <br><br>Other than that, my other issue was:<br><br><i>
  <blockquote> “Fern doesn’t have a clue how pretty she is. That makes her priceless.” </blockquote>
</i><br><i>
  <blockquote> “And because she was unaware, she became more appealing still.” </blockquote>
</i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495995592ra/22873464.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Why? Why is Fern more beautiful simply because she’s unaware of it? Why does her lack of confidence make her more desirable?? Was Ambrose less desirable when he was aware of his good-looks? Because the story certainly doesn’t indicate that. <br><br>I dislike this ideal that women need to just look beautiful effortlessly and act blissfully unaware. I'm not saying every character needs fantastic self-confidence, and this wouldn't have made sense for Fern's character. But why romanticize a lack of self-esteem??<br><br><b>In Conclusion:</b><br><br>Beautiful and captivating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7746427393014154318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_720790177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/720790177" />
    <a title="Jess-i-ca ~Sometimes a Gif Witch~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8740772-jess-i-ca-sometimes-a-gif-witch"><img alt="Jess-i-ca ~Sometimes a Gif Witch~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487382075p2/8740772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/720790177?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess-i-ca ~Sometimes a Gif Witch~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess-i-ca ~Sometimes a Gif Witch~" href="/user/show/8740772-jess-i-ca-sometimes-a-gif-witch">Jess-i-ca ~Sometimes a Gif Witch~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8740772-jess-i-ca-sometimes-a-gif-witch?shelf=v-is-for-virgin">v-is-for-virgin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8740772-jess-i-ca-sometimes-a-gif-witch?shelf=my-absolute-favorites">my-absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8740772-jess-i-ca-sometimes-a-gif-witch?shelf=made-me-boo-hoo">made-me-boo-hoo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8740772-jess-i-ca-sometimes-a-gif-witch?shelf=bad-ass-heroine">bad-ass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer720790177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4569032055313511950"><i>
  <b>5 Overcoming Stars!<br/><br/>”Victory is in the battle” </b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382555437ra/5985657.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Wow this book… What can I say other than it just moved me in ways that I didn’t expect… I laughed, I cried, my heart broke for the characters. I as well as most every other girl has felt a case of UGS growing up. I knew a boy who suffered from MD. I was 18 and just starting college when the September 11, 2001 attack happened. I know how that day affected me. I know people who joined the military and went off to war as a result of the attacks and </span>
  <span id="freeText4569032055313511950" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>5 Overcoming Stars!<br><br>”Victory is in the battle” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382555437ra/5985657.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wow this book… What can I say other than it just moved me in ways that I didn’t expect… I laughed, I cried, my heart broke for the characters. I as well as most every other girl has felt a case of UGS growing up. I knew a boy who suffered from MD. I was 18 and just starting college when the September 11, 2001 attack happened. I know how that day affected me. I know people who joined the military and went off to war as a result of the attacks and I have seen the effects is has put on people who have return as well as their families. It's like I just felt everything that happened in this book......<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382555943ra/5986246.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is one of those books that it breaks your heart but is so worth reading!<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/cotejb/media/FUNNY%202/4973548_zps836cc80b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382545801ra/5977300.gif" alt=" photo 4973548_zps836cc80b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Fern suffers from Ugly Girl Syndrome (UGS) but has a heart made of gold. She is awkward but funny and so pure at the same time. She’s just a great human being in general.<br><br><i>
  <b>"If God makes all our faces, did he laugh when he made me?" </b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/cotejb/media/FUNNY%202/tumblr_lv3b5s8tKG1qd85a3_zpse20d2b56.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382545801ra/5977301.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_lv3b5s8tKG1qd85a3_zpse20d2b56.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She takes care of her cousin, Bailey, who unfortunately suffers from Muscular Dystrophy (MD) and is wheelchair bound. Bailey is hands down one of the BEST supporting characters ever! LOVED HIM! He has an absolutely wonderful sense of humor and you put him and Fern together and they have the best time…<br><br><i>
  <b>"I’ve got Rocky Road Ice cream. It looks a little like poop. Can we become one with Rocky Road instead?”<br>	“It does look a little like shit. Nuts and everything. Count me in.” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382557169ra/5987161.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They assist Bailey’s dad Coach Sheen with his wrestling stuff and that’s how they grow up with Ambrose Young. Ambrose is a superstar in the wrestling world as well as hot stuff around the school. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382558105i/5988118.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fern is in love with him and has been since they were 10. Unfortunately he isn't attracted to her.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/cotejb/media/FUNNY%202/Heshot_zps8d777ec1.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425933ra/850441.gif" alt="hot photo Heshot_zps8d777ec1.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>After high school is out, Ambrose (aka Brosey, Brose, Hercules) decides to enlist in the army. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382555437ra/5985658.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He comes back from the war a changed person.<br><br><i>
  <b>”The lucky ones are the ones who don’t come back.” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382556515ra/5986731.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fern along with Bailey, help Ambrose accept who he is and remember who he was.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/cotejb/media/FUNNY%202/tumblr_mqq5co7pE31qlzvdto1_500_zps98b85dc1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
