<span id="freeTextContainer7606639163879550553"><b>5 Stars and Beyond (2013)<br/>* * * * * <i>Spoiler Free-Thank you to all of the previous reviewers and a special shout out to Mo for personally recommending this book to me.</i><br/>Books provide a lot of purposes for us, in my opinion. <br/><br/>Some educate. <br/><br/>Some take us to a place of fantasy with the use of otherworldly places and characters; allowing us to experience things not possible in this existence.<br/> <br/>Some present sweet concepts of love, happiness, and family with very little hardship and a perfect ending.<br/><br/>All of t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7606639163879550553" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars and Beyond (2013)<br>* * * * * <i>Spoiler Free-Thank you to all of the previous reviewers and a special shout out to Mo for personally recommending this book to me.</i><br>Books provide a lot of purposes for us, in my opinion. <br><br>Some educate. <br><br>Some take us to a place of fantasy with the use of otherworldly places and characters; allowing us to experience things not possible in this existence.<br> <br>Some present sweet concepts of love, happiness, and family with very little hardship and a perfect ending.<br><br>All of the types mentioned allow us to be in the moment consumed with the story... becoming as involved as we wish. <br><br>Then there is the type of book which forces the reader to pay attention. To feel deeply what the characters are feeling. To relate to hopes, desires, dreams, and pain so sincerely, you feel as if it is actually happening to real people, not characters in a book.<br><br>Making Faces was that type of book for me.</b><br><br>Using the backdrop of Small Town America; creating people whose lives intertwined and developed over years; having the collective hope of the community rest on the shoulders of heroic boy/man and him feeling the burden and responsibilities... all of these elements and so much more made for a perfect storm of emotions.<br><br>I really feel this is a book that has the ability to cause a person to think about what is important - what really counts in life and how we regard one another. <br><br>There is tremendous beauty in this story and my true desire is for you to read it fresh. If you wish more, my updates express my feelings while reading this amazing book. These updates are so descriptive, I was moved so.. they are like a review chapter by chapter. <br><br>Please see all of the detailed reviews out there; they are so personal and descriptive, I know you will find the one which will connect with you. <br><br>Don't be put off because you may feel while reading it. Sometimes, that is what called for in our lives... here's to feeling without reserve.<br><br><strong>For more Reviews, Free E-books and Giveaways</strong><br><div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23173697-ida?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2333610705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15405503231748724847">This book was painful, beautiful, sad and heartwarming all at once. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522507368ra/25301632.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/>Ambrose Young is beautiful. Hercules beautiful. With his dark hair that touches his shoulders, muscular body and eyes that burn right through you. <br/>Fern taylor is quite the opposite. <br/>With her pail and small body, short, red and curly hair she looks more like Annie than a high school student. Because they were so different, Fern loved Ambrose from afar, thinking someone like him could never love someone like her... until he wa</span>
  <span id="freeText15405503231748724847" style="display:none">This book was painful, beautiful, sad and heartwarming all at once. <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522507368ra/25301632.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Ambrose Young is beautiful. Hercules beautiful. With his dark hair that touches his shoulders, muscular body and eyes that burn right through you. <br>Fern taylor is quite the opposite. <br>With her pail and small body, short, red and curly hair she looks more like Annie than a high school student. Because they were so different, Fern loved Ambrose from afar, thinking someone like him could never love someone like her... until he wasn't beautiful anymore.<br><br><blockquote> <i> Lost or Alone? <br>Ambrose said alone, and Fern responded, “I would much rather be lost with you than alone without you, so I choose lost with a caveat.” <br>Ambrose responded, “No caveats,” to which Fern replied, “Then lost, because alone feels permanent, and lost can be found.” </i> </blockquote><br>I've only ever read one other book by Amy Harmon, but what was clear then, and became even more clear now, is that she truly has a unique ability to create characters you just can help but love.<br>Fern is not my typical heroin, but I loved her selflessness, her love for her friends and family, her quick mind and sense of humor.<br>I loved Bailey. I loved Ambrose. I loved Rita, Jesse, Paulie, Grant and even Beans. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530548184ra/25910226.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Everybody is a main character to someone,” Bailey theorized. <br>“There are no minor characters.”</i>
</blockquote><br>As with a lot of Amy Harmons books, she alternates her writing between the past and the present, and the story is told by several characters. This lets us experience what it was like for the characters growing up, and also take part in some of the moments you can see truly define how they become as adults. Such as Fern realising she's not considered pretty, or some of the huge moments concerning Bailey that I will not spoil for you, but they were heartbreaking. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Because sometimes we fall in love with a face and not what’s behind it.”</i>
</blockquote><br>It was a heartbreaking journey filled with loss, love, broken souls, friendship and heroisme, and it's a book I can wholeheartedly recommend!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“How did you know I needed you?” Fern whispered in broken tones. <br>“Because I needed you,” Ambrose confessed </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518475812ra/25048631.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1246671211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1246671211" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1246671211?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781492976424" href="/book/show/18700870-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=read-it-and-weep">read-it-and-weep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1246671211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer145377256828489525">I'm gonna start this review off with an embarrassing confession... I read the first 10% of this book at home, then the next 89% of it at work, and then the last 1% of it in the car on the way home from work... I had like three pages left and I just had to know what happened so as soon at I hit the red light near the EarthFare I knew it was my chance to read the last three pages... Bad move on my part. As I read the last few sentences I started balling my eyes out and completely forgetting I was </span>
  <span id="freeText145377256828489525" style="display:none">I'm gonna start this review off with an embarrassing confession... I read the first 10% of this book at home, then the next 89% of it at work, and then the last 1% of it in the car on the way home from work... I had like three pages left and I just had to know what happened so as soon at I hit the red light near the EarthFare I knew it was my chance to read the last three pages... Bad move on my part. As I read the last few sentences I started balling my eyes out and completely forgetting I was at a stop, until the guy behind me honked his horn at me bringing me back to life. <br><br>Making Faces was just that amazing. It makes you want to read between red lights and at any chance you can get. Making Faces surrounds three main characters. Fern is the girl who is forever overlooked. She's the bookwork, small, sweet, with red hair. Bailey, Ferns cousin and best friend, is the sweet caring boy who is suffering from muscle dystrophy. And Ambrose Young, school's star athlete and overall talented guy. Fern has admired Ambrose from afar for as long as she can remember, and he only notices her after an odd event plays out. But even after that things seem to go back to the way they were. That is until 9/11 happens and it hit Ambrose in a way he didn't see coming. Even though he is so gifted he still feels like he needs to do more. He decides to sign up for the military and to serve in Iraq and talks his four friends into coming with him.<br><br>That's where the story will takes off, because Ambrose is the only one who returns, but even he doesn't come back in one piece. Ambrose and Fern's relationship is the definition of hope. Their relationship is sweet, playful, and deep. Harmon again writes such strong leading characters and gives them so much depth. Fern, though shy is far from weak. Ambrose who to the eye is strong is so weak. Them being opposites gave this book such balance. I liked that Fern shows him that there is more to life and a person than what meets the eye. That you can either run and hide or face things head on. That it's okay to let people in. That looks might be the thing that originally draws you to a person, but it's not the thing that keeps you there. Their relationship shows you that being together is a give and take situation but you both have to be willing to do both. You have to know when to push and when to ease up. Their relationship is such gold.<br><br><i> "You are still beautiful," Fern says softly "I think that statement is more a reflection of your beauty than mine."</i><br><br>Even with these two character being as amazing as they are there is no doubt who stole the show... Bailey. His and Fern's friendship is probably, if not, my favorite friendship I've ever read. There aren't even words to describe how amazing it is. Everything that comes out of his mouth is written with such a force. He is unlike any character I've ever had the pleasure of reading. He alone would be a reason I would recommend this book. The characters in <i>Making Faces</i> are flawless.<br><br>The plot of this book is so different. At first with how everything was laid out I didn't think I would like it. The timeline bounces around from the past the present, and I didn't think thing would come together... But when they do, and everything is reveal, it is mind blowing. Everything from the flashbacks, the old stories, the current events, the title of the chapters are so well thought out. When I started too figure everything out I was taken back by how incredible this truly was. Even when there were a few moments towards the end when I knew what was going to happen next, and things were playing of cliche, the ending itself made up for anything that could have happened. The last few paragraphs made up for anything that would ever be lacking.<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-SaWA2arAcN4/VTzgmWRVKNI/AAAAAAAABlw/4MDgdBfzpHY/s1600/11454051.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="156" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457394355i/18354399.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I think writing reviews on books you love is so much harder then doing to for ones you hate. You can never seem to perfectly put into words how it made you feel. <i>Making Faces </i>is heartbreaking and heartwarming. <i>Making Faces </i>will probably be one of my top reads this year. This book broke my heart in the best way possible.<br><br>It's a book with so many layers, and so many lovely messages. This is a book that is tattooed on me and will forever leave a lasting impression.<br><br><i>"True beauty, the kind that doesn't fade or wash off, takes time. It takes incredible endurance. It is the slow drip that creates the stalactite, the shaking of the Earth that creates mountains, the <br>constant pounding of the waves that breaks up the rocks and smooths the rough edges. And from the violence, the furor, the raging of the winds, the roaring of the waters, something better emerges, something that would have otherwise never existed. <b>And so we endure. We have faith <br>that there is purpose. We hope for things we can't see. We believe there are lessons in loss, power in love, and that we have within us the potential for a beauty so magnificent, our bodies can't contain it."</b></i><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="145377256828489525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_747548770" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/747548770" />
    <a title="Crystal~BIG book addict~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7270157-crystal-big-book-addict"><img alt="Crystal~BIG book addict~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375663139p2/7270157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/747548770?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal~BIG book addict~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal~BIG book addict~" href="/user/show/7270157-crystal-big-book-addict">Crystal~BIG book addict~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781301673872" href="/book/show/18301124-making-faces">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer747548770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1906616837470559835"><b>5 Absolutely Beautiful Stars!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383181501ra/6429893.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>This is one of the best books I have read in awhile. So what was it about?<br/><br/><b>Family, Friends and Faith</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383181501i/6429894.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Was there a romance? Absolutely, but to me that played a secondary role.<br/><br/><br/><b>Fern</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379787022i/490536.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Fern was always the ugly duckling growing up. She has red, curly hair, big teeth, scrawny and freckles. She made up for her looks in personality and smarts. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>God has given you one face and you make yourself another. ~Hamlet</b>
</i><br/><br/>Fern has been in love with Ambrose since she was 10 years old. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>To F</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText1906616837470559835" style="display:none"><b>5 Absolutely Beautiful Stars!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383181501ra/6429893.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This is one of the best books I have read in awhile. So what was it about?<br><br><b>Family, Friends and Faith</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383181501i/6429894.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Was there a romance? Absolutely, but to me that played a secondary role.<br><br><br><b>Fern</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379787022i/490536.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fern was always the ugly duckling growing up. She has red, curly hair, big teeth, scrawny and freckles. She made up for her looks in personality and smarts. <br><br><i>
  <b>God has given you one face and you make yourself another. ~Hamlet</b>
</i><br><br>Fern has been in love with Ambrose since she was 10 years old. <br><br><i>
  <b>To Fern, Ambrose Young was absolutely beautiful, a Greek God among mortals, the stuff of fairy tales and movie screens.</b>
</i><br><br>Fern eventually grows into her looks and blossoms into a beautiful young woman.<br><br><br><b>Ambrose</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379800265i/666632.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ambrose is gorgeous, athletic, popular and smart. He is the captain of the wrestling team. Fern's friend Rita wants to ask him out by writing him a love note. She asks Fern to help her and things progress from there. Ambrose continues to write Rita love notes and then Fern answers them. Eventually, he finds out that it wasn't Rita writing them and that it was Fern. He's hurt and confused because he really liked the girl in the notes.<br><br>During their senior year in high school, the tragedy of 9/11 occurred. At the end of their senior year, Ambrose talks to his friends about joining the National Guard and they all agree to join. Five leave for war, only one comes home. Ambrose returns home scarred both emotionally and physically. One side of his face has been horribly disfigured.<br><br>Fern tries to bring him out of his self loathing and misery. Eventually he slowly starts to come out of his shell and his feelings for Fern grow deeper.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>"Everything has changed! You are beautiful, I am hideous, you don't need me anymore, but I sure as hell need you!" ~Ambrose<br><br>"You make me feel safe, Fern. You make me forget. And when I kiss you I just want to keep kissing you. Everything else falls away. It's the only peace I've found..."</b>
</i><br><br><br><b>Bailey</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383181501i/6429895.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To me, Bailey was the star of the book. He and Fern are cousins and best friends. He also has muscular dystrophy so is in a wheelchair. Fern is always with Bailey, helping to take care of him, driving around and companion. He was such a special person in this book. His humor and the way he dealt with his disease made me smile. <br><br><i>
  <b>"But there are times when you just need to acknowledge the shit, Fern, you know...Own it, wallow in it, become one with the shit."</b>
</i><br><br><br>This is one of those books that I think everyone needs to read at least once. It was beautiful and heartwarming, tragic and heartbreaking and overall an absolute joy to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1906616837470559835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IT9l4SS2J0mdmzofSBttQ/OhyEHPanNVqB87KmQ2rJHpM4Tcsl2mRKK8GjLtd4rl+t5R15YlitTwOJIR8rC82w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VXeMK/u6AZsf1bIUVXVSQD3iEns9eKwAJDNRYd5DRE2de20WbVGAliDykjnwGbXmNJ2L7WQ3VYF8FPhaSMVUBw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon">About Amy Harmon</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1341709289p3/5829056.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2685080690747382610">Amy Harmon is a Wall Street Journal, USA Today, and New York Times Bestselling author. Amy knew at an early age that writing was something she wanted to do, and she divided her time between writing songs and stories as she grew. Having grown up in the middle of wheat fields without a television, with only her books and her siblings to entertain her, she developed a strong sense of what made a good</span>
  <span id="freeText2685080690747382610" style="display:none">Amy Harmon is a Wall Street Journal, USA Today, and New York Times Bestselling author. Amy knew at an early age that writing was something she wanted to do, and she divided her time between writing songs and stories as she grew. Having grown up in the middle of wheat fields without a television, with only her books and her siblings to entertain her, she developed a strong sense of what made a good story. Her books are now being published in eighteen languages, truly a dream come true for a little country girl from Levan, Utah.<br /><br />Amy Harmon has written fifteen novels including the USA Today Bestsellers, Making Faces and Running Barefoot, as well as The Law of Moses, Infinity + One and the New York Times Bestseller, A Different Blue. Her fantasy novel, The Bird and the Sword, was a Goodreads Book of the Year finalist. Her newest release, What the Wind Knows, is an Amazon charts bestseller. For updates on upcoming book releases, author posts and more, join Amy at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.authoramyharmon.com">www.authoramyharmon.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2685080690747382610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/25789248-making-faces">Quotes from Making Faces</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;If God made all our faces, did he laugh when he made me?<br /><br />Does he make the legs that cannot walk and eyes that cannot see?<br /><br />Does he curl the hair upon my head 'til it rebels in wild defiance?<br /><br />Does he close the ears of a deaf man to make him more reliant?<br /><br />Is the way I look a coincidence or just a twist of fate?<br /><br />If he made me this way, is it okay, to blame him for the things I hate?<br /><br />For the flaws that seem to worsen every time I see a mirror,For the ugliness I see in me, for the loathing and the fear.<br /><br />Does he sculpt us for his pleasure, for a reason I can't see?<br /><br />If God makes all our faces, did he laugh when he made me?&rdquo;</span>
